It is the path of yin yielding to yang once more, the way of withered blossoms blooming anew.

The "lead-flower" is the radiance of the Dao-heart’s true knowing. *Gui*-water is the selfish desire of the human heart’s guest qi. When the lead-flower appears, the Dao-heart remains undimmed; when *gui*-water is exhausted, the human heart abides in stillness. With the Dao-heart undimmed and the human heart still, the original, unblemished, and perfectly complete true numen reappears—thus the blossoms, though fallen, bloom again in full.

Because *gui*-water must be spent, it is said: *"Gathered beneath the moon’s waning light."* Because the lead-flower must appear, it is said: *"Mend the robe in morning’s glow."* The selfish desires of the human heart are like the guest qi from without, like the moon’s waning light. The true knowing of the Dao-heart is the original, upright qi, like the sun’s radiance. Gathering beneath the moon’s waning light sweeps away the selfish desires of the human heart—this is the retreat of yin. Mending the robe in morning’s glow gradually replenishes the true knowing of the Dao-heart—this is the advance of yang.

Retreat yin until not a trace of yin qi remains—only then is the waning light fully gathered. Advance yang until yang qi is utterly pure—only then is the robe fully mended. With yin spent and yang complete, one returns to the origin and reverts to the root; the original face is fully revealed. Is not the rebirth of fallen blossoms a true saying? This celestial mechanism of withered blossoms blooming anew is rarely known in the world. To know it, one must ponder its beginning and end alongside the immortals.

[Li’s Explanation]
Wu Yuan’s annotation is excellent in principle, yet it does not address the core meaning of this chapter. Here, the discussion pertains to the nurturing of the returned elixir. "Flight" refers to ascent and descent, signifying the morning advance of yang fire and the evening retreat of yin tally. "Shedding" means the elixir has taken form, leaves have fallen to return to the root—this directly points to the restoration of life.

After life is restored, one draws upon the external furnace’s metal-water, extracts lead, and replenishes mercury to nurture the spiritual embryo. As *Awakening to Reality* says: *"The external furnace’s increase and decrease require effort."* The *Triple Concordance* states: *"Observe and tend with utmost care, / Examine and adjust cold and warmth, / Cycle through the twelve nodes, / And when each ends, begin anew."* Elder Feng said: *"At midnight and noon, focus the fire’s timing; / At dawn and dusk, bathe the golden elixir in ice."* Thus it is said: *"Once shed, they bloom again at the appointed time."*

The "reblooming" refers to the branches of blossoms in the western garden below. "When the lead-flower appears, as *gui* is spent" means the great medicine of the returned elixir arises after *gui*. When lead is born, it is gathered. Gold, when far from its fullness, is unfit for tasting. Only after the initial surge of *gui*-water on the five thousand forty-eighth day does one carefully apply effort, seize the foremost treasure of the first tide—this is the supreme method.

When *gui* arises, it is the fourteenth; when *gui* is spent, it is the fifteenth—at this very moment, a single ray of yang light appears. In the human body, this is nothing other than the great movement within the great stillness. Gather and swallow it, and the returned elixir is formed. Yet once the great elixir is obtained, external lead arises anew, and the alchemist must take it for the purpose of gentle nurturing. Thus it is said: *"Once more, the western garden’s branches bloom full with flowers."*

Just as one faces the moon to gather and put away—this is the drawing of lead—so too does one turn toward the morning sun to mend the patched robe—this is the replenishing of mercury. The method of gathering requires clarity on the moon’s waxing and waning, hence the reference to "facing the moon"; the method of mending demands the use of the sun’s dawn and dusk, hence the metaphor of the "morning sun." Such are the subtle truths of the mysterious arts. These profound subtleties are rarely known in the world. Should one wish to understand them, one must seek them through careful inquiry with a realized immortal—only then may one avoid error.

**[Liu’s Verse]**
The Moon-Couch Furnace.
**[Li’s Verse]**
The Heavenly Treasure.

The rootless tree blooms in full,
Plucked from the Moon-Couch Furnace.
Prolonging life, dispelling calamity,
Best to forge good bonds and prepare the dharma-wealth.
From this, the Heavenly Treasure may be achieved—
Let the deluded masses mock my folly.

Urge the worthy to abandon cunning,
Without a wise teacher, do not force guesses.

**[Liu’s Annotation]**
The treasure of primordial true spirit is formless and imageless, without direction or place—from where, then, is it gathered to congeal the returned elixir? Though formless and imageless, without direction or place, it too has its time of blooming. When that time arrives, within the indistinct there is form; within the profound darkness, there is essence. Its essence is most true, and within it lies constancy. Its symbolic form resembles the Moon-Couch. Common practitioners, unaware of the ancients’ intent in taking this image, misidentify it as the space between the kidneys, or the bright hall between the brows, or the stubborn fleshly heart. Even worse are the demonic fabrications that point to a woman’s birth passage—gross errors, all!

What is meant by the "Moon-Couch"? It is the moon in its reclining aspect. Each month, on the third day, beneath the dark body of the southwest *kun* earth, the crescent’s light emerges, its glow reclining—hence the name "Moon-Couch." In the hexagrams, this is the faint yang beginning to arise beneath pure yin, the *Fu* hexagram. In the human being, it is the movement after extreme stillness, the birth of brightness in an empty chamber, the stirring of the heart of Heaven and Earth. Within this heart lies a single point of primordial ancestral *qi*, faintly revealing its signs from the depths of darkness, resembling the reclining light of the moon. Because this single point of ancestral *qi* is the root of Heaven and Earth, the origin of the Five Phases, it can create immortals and buddhas, forge sages and worthies, and secure both nature and life—thus it is also called the Moon-Couch Furnace.

This heart of Heaven and Earth aligns its virtue with Heaven and Earth, its brightness with the sun and moon, its order with the four seasons, and its auspices with spirits and gods—rarely encountered, difficult to meet. Should one chance upon it, the moment must not be missed. One must swiftly reach out to pluck it, seal it securely, and guard against leakage. Thus may life be prolonged and calamities dispelled. Yet such matters of prolonging life and dispelling calamity cannot be undertaken by those without great merit and conduct, nor accomplished by those lacking great resolve and strength. One must externally cultivate good affinities to refine virtue, and internally prepare dharma-wealth with sincerity—only then can one move the Imperial Ultimate and obtain the Heavenly Treasure.

Dharma-wealth is not worldly wealth, but the wealth within the dharma: single-minded devotion, true practice, and unwavering resolve—this is the good wealth. As the Perfected One of Upper Yang said: *"If Heaven resists, one must seek it with dharma-wealth and utmost sincerity. For to seek the Heavenly Treasure, one must exhaust human effort. If human effort is not exhausted, there is no dharma-wealth. Without dharma-wealth, to vainly desire the Heavenly Treasure is difficult indeed."* How can one seeking the Heavenly Treasure fail to first prepare dharma-wealth?

The Heavenly Treasure is no other thing than the golden elixir refined from true spirit, the returned elixir restored to the heart of Heaven and Earth. "True spirit" and "heart of Heaven and Earth" refer to it before refinement; "Heavenly Treasure" and "golden elixir" refer to it after refinement and maturation. Once the Heavenly Treasure is obtained, the ten thousand things are all empty, the roots and dust are transformed, and one enters the state of unknowing, without self or others—let the deluded masses mock my folly.

This folly must be transmitted orally by a wise teacher, heart to heart—it cannot be known through forced guesses. As the Immortal Elder said: *"Urge the worthy to abandon cunning; without a wise teacher, do not force guesses."* How greatly he warns later generations!

**[Li’s Explanation]**
"Blooms" refers to the jade bud’s first arising. The Moon-Couch Furnace has no fixed location in the human body, nor a fixed time, for it appears when yang *qi* first stirs, light within stillness—thus it is compared to the new moon born from extreme darkness. This moon in the sky has its *geng* direction and its third day, both with specific times and places. But in the human body, where it appears is the *geng* direction, and when it appears is the third day—it cannot be predetermined.

What is the shape of the Moon-Couch? It is as depicted in Liu’s diagram: reclining, with nine parts black and one part white, the white seen within the black, yang *qi* first arising—thus the white light appears above as the Moon-Couch. What people today describe has this shape, but it is the *upright* moon, not the *reclining* moon.

Why speak of "plucking it down"? Because its *qi* is in the void. When the alchemist sees this thread of white light, one must not rashly activate the river chariot. One should only, with a tranquil spirit and harmonious intent, gather it from where the *qi* arises—hence the phrase *"plucked from the Moon-Couch Furnace."* When spirit and *qi* unite, suddenly the yang light shines fully, like the full circle of the fifteenth day ○—this is the mid-autumn moon, the tide of *qi* at its peak. Only then does one drive it along the Yellow Path and send it to the Yellow Court. From this, life may be prolonged and calamities dispelled.

True companions of the Dharma and wealth are those of like mind who cherish the Dao, willingly offer their good fortune, protect the Dharma for others, and assist in their attainment of the Way. In *Discernments on Cultivating the Real*, Wu Yuan’s commentary on this chapter likewise interprets "Dharma-wealth" as something within the body—this is merely a corrective against greed. Speaking impartially, Dharma-wealth has two aspects: the inner Dharma-wealth, which is true gold, and the outer Dharma-wealth, which is a provisional treasure. Though borrowing the provisional to refine the true is indispensable, one should not covet it excessively.

When the celestial treasure is refined, one may feign foolishness and play the fool, holding jade within and embracing the uncarved block. Though the deluded masses may mock me as a simpleton, all such matters may be dismissed without concern. Yet how easily can one speak of refining the celestial treasure! Without encountering an enlightened teacher, one cannot know its secrets.

**Liu’s Verse:**
The Reverted Elixir ripens.

**Li’s Verse:**
The Reverted Elixir enters the mountains.
The rootless tree, its blossoms now full,
Bears fruit, its harvest complete in every flavor.
Like a crimson tangerine, round as a pellet,
Guard and defend its embankments—never neglect.
Learn the method of plants gathering their crowns,
Return to life, revert to the root, restore the origin.

**Liu’s Annotation:**
The treasure of true numen—what departs returns, what is old becomes new again, unharmed and undiminished, still the original substance—this is the fullness of the blossom. "Fullness" here speaks of the fruit’s harvest, its flavors complete. When the Golden Elixir is accomplished, the Five Phases cluster together, the Four Images harmonize, and benevolence, righteousness, propriety, wisdom, and trust merge into one principle. Essence, spirit, ethereal soul, corporeal soul, and intent return to a single *qi*. Further refined by the fire of talismans, it becomes a purely yang substance—lively and fluid, crimson as a tangerine, round as a pellet. At this time, one must guard its embankments, never neglecting vigilance in the twelve hours, concealing one’s brilliance and nurturing obscurity. Learn the method of plants gathering their crowns, return to life, revert to the root, and restore the origin, awaiting the stillness that gives rise to movement. Then, uniting with the primordial, one completes the Great Reversion Elixir. This speaks of the work of forging the Great Elixir after the Reverted Elixir is accomplished.

For the Reverted Elixir merely restores the original substance of one’s own nature—an affair of transcending the mundane. As Lü Zu said: *"With three leads, only one lead is secured; the golden fruit and immortal sprout have yet to take form."* The Great Elixir, however, is the upward endeavor pursued after the Reverted Elixir—a matter of entering sagehood. As Lü Zu said: *"Reinstall the furnace, reset the crucible, ride the tiger and mount the dragon to leave the mortal realm."* If one only refines the Reverted Elixir without forging the Great Elixir, one merely completes the initial vehicle of the Dao, becoming nothing more than a whole person—how could one enter the realm of the sages?

The "selecting of a numinous site" and "establishing of a Dao hermitage" do not refer to external places but to the numinous site and Dao hermitage within. When cultivation reaches the point of reverting to the root and restoring life, the work of the Reverted Elixir is complete. Nurturing and warming it, when spirit and *qi* are abundant, the elixir becomes numinous—this is called the Numinous Elixir. From this numinous site, reinstall the furnace and reset the crucible—this is called establishing the Dao hermitage. "Selecting a numinous site" means awaiting the arising of the first yang. This first yang is the yang of primordial stillness giving rise to movement, unlike the yang of the Reverted Elixir, which arises from the postnatal to become primordial. Though both are primordial, there is a distinction of before and after. To complete the Great Reversion Elixir, one must unite with the yang within the primordial—without this, success is impossible. Thus it is said: *"Uniting with the primordial completes the Great Reversion."*

Only when the Great Elixir is accomplished does one lay the foundation of sagehood. If the Great Elixir remains unformed, it is but a halfway endeavor, not the full achievement of cultivation. As the Buddhist scriptures say: *"One who halts at the hundred-foot pole has entered but not truly arrived. Advance another step at the hundred-foot pole, and the ten directions become one’s entire body."* Does this not speak of completing the Great Reversion?

**Li’s Explanation:**
"Full" refers to the Reverted Elixir, signifying the reunion of nature and emotions. Its method lies in attaining emptiness and guarding stillness. Observe the moon’s waxing in the west—it is like the initial stirring of yang *qi*. Immediately mobilize one’s own mercury to meet it, where external contact sparks internal resonance, and internal touch evokes external response, like a magnet drawing iron. Gather it into the cinnabar field—this is the external elixir. The method is exceedingly simple and easy, so the ancient immortals said: *"It can be accomplished in less than half an hour."*

The Elixir has two grades, which may be divided into three vehicles. The methods of the three vehicles all involve gathering the lead blossom and are all called Reverted Elixirs, differing only in their scale and sequence.

The first is the initial vehicle, called the Coagulated Elixir or Jade Fluid Reverted Elixir. Within the postnatal, it returns to the primordial, departing from *gui* to take *ren*, nurturing it with jade fluid to round the inner elixir—this is the study of fulfilling one’s nature, the immortal of humanity.

The second is the superior vehicle, named the Reverted Elixir or Sevenfold Return. Using the primordial returned from the postnatal, it plants the seed of the primordial, establishing the Elixir Mother—this is the study of establishing one’s life, the immortal of earth.

The third is the great vehicle, called the Ninefold Cyclical Great Reversion Elixir. Its medicine is likened to the full moon of the fifteenth night. Within the primordial, it is primordial; when the fire arrives, it moves, transforming into white fluid. Swallowed into the abdomen, it congeals into something supremely firm—this is the Golden Fluid Reverted Elixir, most numinous and wondrous, perfecting sagehood and realizing transcendence. This is the study of uniting nature and life, the immortal of heaven.

"The blossoms now full" refers to the foundation of the superior vehicle’s elixir. Having formed one fruit and reaped one harvest, its method of refining lead involves the mutual absorption of two substances, with the Five Phases all complete—this is what is meant by "flavors complete." Though this elixir is not that of the great vehicle, it is nonetheless vividly crimson like a tangerine and perfectly round like a pellet. At this stage, one must silently attend to it, continuously preserving it as if it were always present. Otherwise, if one’s embrace is not intimate, it may easily slip away. Thus, one must guard its embankments and never neglect vigilance.

Learn the method of gathering herbs and bringing cultivation to completion—this is what the *Yi* means by "therewith wash the heart, storing it in secrecy." Returning to life, reverting to the root, and restoring the primordial—this is what the *Cantong Qi* means by "the true dwelling in whiteness, square and round within an inch."

Choose a numinous site and establish a Daoist hermitage. Wu Yuan states that the numinous site and Daoist hermitage reside within the human body, yet they also serve dual functions, inner and outer. For the inner numinous site and hermitage, one must seek clarity and stillness in the spirit terrace, with harmonious qi and spirit, and therein establish the Peaceful Hermitage of the Daoist’s heart. For the outer numinous site and hermitage, one must seek blessed mountains and auspicious lands, free from the disturbance of worldly dust, and therein establish the Thatched Hut of White Clouds for the Daoist. In this way, both the heart and its traces remain pure, true power fills to the brim, yang is born within lead, and through gathering and uniting, the Dao is accomplished in the ninefold great return—thus the sagely work is perfected.

**Liu’s Note:** The qi of true oneness.
**Li’s Note:** The place of union.

The rootless tree—its blossoms now flourishing—speaks of the rootless as though it had roots. The three talents’ apertures, the essence of the two and five: when heaven and earth unite, the myriad things are born; when sun and moon unite, cold and heat follow in order; when man and woman unite, conception begins. How clear this is, yet when explained to you, I fear you may meet it and still fail to recognize it truly.

**Liu’s Commentary:** The treasure of the primordial true numinous, possessing all principles and responding to all affairs, still and unmoving, yet when stimulated, penetrating all—nowhere obstructed, nowhere not efficacious—this is the flourishing of the blossoms. Since the blossoms flourish, though the tree is rootless, the blossoms nonetheless have roots. What root is this? It is the aperture of the three talents—heaven, earth, and humanity—and the essence of the wondrous union of yin-yang and the Five Phases. Because it is the aperture of the three talents and the essence of the two and five, it is born prior to heaven and earth yet concealed within them afterward. One qi divides into yin and yang, and yin and yang unite to form one qi. Thus, when heaven and earth’s yin and yang above and below unite, they merge into one qi and the myriad things are born; when the sun and moon’s yin and yang come and go in union, they merge into one qi and cold and heat follow in order; when man and woman’s yin and yang unite with one another, conception begins. Observing heaven and earth, sun and moon, man and woman—only when one yin and one yang unite is there creation. From this, one may know that the Dao of nature and life cannot be completed without the union of yin and yang into one. This one qi is the root of nature and life, the aperture of life and death. With this aperture, yin and yang unite and life is born; without this qi, yin and yang turn away from one another and death ensues. Human life and death lie solely in the presence or absence of this one qi. Yet people do not know what this qi is or where it resides. Some mistake it for the qi of breath, or circulate it upward and downward in the Yellow Court, or gather it in the cinnabar field, or concentrate it between the brows, or collect it in the Celestial Valley, or amass it behind the brain—endless strange and fantastical notions, all ultimately leading to emptiness and loss. They do not realize that the primordial true oneness qi is invisible, inaudible, and intangible. The sage shapes the real through the empty, manifests the existent through the nonexistent. The real and existent are true yin and true yang; the empty and nonexistent are the qi of the two eights’ waxing and waning. When these two are juxtaposed, one qi resides in the center, congealing into the elixir—this is an endeavor of the empty void. How could it be guessed at through forms and images? How could it be sought in apertures with fixed locations? Since the Immortal Elder saw that people did not recognize this one qi, he pointed to the apertures of the three talents and the essence of the two and five, and further illustrated it through the union of heaven and earth, sun and moon, man and woman, clearly indicating this one qi to all. Yet he feared that when people encountered this one qi, they might fail to recognize it even when face to face. With boldness and at risk of censure, I, Wu Yuan, shall now vividly convey the Immortal Elder’s meaning for all to hear. Know that the primordial true oneness qi is no other thing—it is the qi of a single point of true numinosity. Because this qi is firm, strong, centered, and upright, it is called true oneness; because it is easy to know and simple in its efficacy, it is called true numinosity. True oneness and true numinosity are utterly without impurity, hence they are called primordial things. True oneness and true numinosity emerge from the same source under different names—they are not two separate things. Does anyone truly recognize this?

**Li’s Explanation:** "Flourishing" means unobstructed. The unobstructed qi emerges from the "union" in the following text. Blossoms grow from the tree, the tree grows from the root, and the root grows from nothingness—thus the rootless has roots. The rootless root is the root that generates heaven, earth, and humanity. This root is a single aperture of emptiness and nothingness, hence it is called the aperture of the three talents. This aperture is the place of essence-union, thus it is said: "the three talents’ apertures, the essence of the two and five." The two and five: heaven’s five is one five, earth’s ten is another five—thus the two and five are two earths, and when the two earths unite, the knife-point elixir is formed. The *Mud Pill* states: "The Mysterious Pass, an aperture no one knows—this is the knife-point elixir, most wondrous and rare." For the place where the two and five unite in essence is the wellspring of elixir production. The great cultivator, recognizing this empty aperture as the place of union, must be able to draw the primordial one qi from the emptiness and nothingness—how great is its function! Thus, when heaven and earth unite, the myriad things are born; when sun and moon unite, cold and heat follow in order; when man and woman unite, conception begins—all evidence of this union. Though this principle is perfectly clear and easily understood by all, in truth, no one understands it. The Immortal Master, in his vast compassion, explains it to you: you need only unite the two qi into one mass where the two eights meet, and the great medicine will be born.

But one fears that when dragon and tiger meet, they may exhale the qi of the two bowstrings, and the elixir-refiner may fail to recognize it truly.

**Liu’s words:** The golden essence flourishes in abundance.
**Li’s words:** Recognize the golden essence.

The rootless tree, its blossoms at their finest—
facing the scene, forget emotion and admire the moon’s radiance.
When the golden essence waxes strong, its brilliance dazzles the eye;
do not, in the garden, mistakenly pluck the wrong melon.
The five metals and eight minerals are all counterfeit;
the myriad herbs and thousand formulas are all amiss.

The golden toad, the jade crow—
recognize them truly, and you are a master of the craft.

**[Liu’s annotation:]**
The primordial numinous treasure is firm and strong, upright and balanced, pure and refined—its blossoms are most excellent. At the time of their finest bloom, when the moon’s radiance unfolds, the golden essence flourishes in abundance, and one should admire it, lest it be lost before one’s eyes. These blossoms open month by month, appearing in season and not out of season, following the lunar cycle with unchanging regularity, their movement and stillness constant, not deviating by even a hair’s breadth.

The golden essence is the luminous essence of metal; in the moon, it is called the moon’s radiance; in man, it is called true essence. True essence is the essence of true numinosity, never dimmed or obscured, and thus it is likened to the moon’s radiance and the golden essence. The true numinosity of man is not easily known, yet it may be understood by observing the truth of the moon and metal; the true numinosity of man is not easily seen, yet it may be perceived in the moon’s radiance and the brilliance of metal.

The essence of all things decays with time, yet the moon’s radiance unfolds month after month, and the golden essence remains undiminished for ten thousand years. Just as the moon’s radiance and the golden essence endure, so too does man’s true essence—though at times it may seem obscured, this is only because postnatal yin qi veils it, while its original substance has never been extinguished.

When the golden essence waxes strong, it is the true essence waxing strong. When the true essence is at its peak, it illumines the world, its qi filling the cosmos—white snow flies across the sky, yellow sprouts cover the earth, golden light dazzles the eye, and wherever one turns, there are blossoms. Yet this true essence is formless and imageless, neither substance nor emptiness; it cannot be sought with intention, nor preserved with non-intention. It can only be grasped spiritually, not spoken of in words. Though it is bright and clear, fully manifest, seen by all, it is recognized by none. It is most difficult to recognize truly, and the cultivator must delve deeply into its subtleties, attaining true knowledge and penetrating insight, before daring to act—lest one mistake the false for the true, the seemingly correct for the genuinely so, and pluck the wrong melon in the garden.

Those blind practitioners of the world, who stumble in their refinement, may suspect the golden essence to be something with form and image, and thus refine the five metals and eight minerals, ingesting the myriad herbs and thousand formulas—things of a different kind from ourselves. How could they ever congeal the elixir and extend their lives? Is this not a grave error?

The toad is a creature of water, belonging to yin; yet when called *golden*, it is the yang within yin, the white within black—this is our true knowing. The crow is a creature that flies above, belonging to yang; yet when called *jade*, it is the yin within yang, the feminine within the masculine—this is our numinous knowing. Only true knowing and numinous knowing are of the same kind as ourselves, the treasures of our nature and life. Taking these two and uniting them to form the elixir, true yet utterly numinous, numinous yet utterly true—true and numinous undispersed, wholly embodying the principle of heaven—neither substance nor emptiness, neither arising nor ceasing: this is what is meant by the moon’s radiance, this is what is meant by the golden essence. When the moon’s radiance unfolds and the golden essence waxes strong, how could one not attain longevity?

Yet most people fail to recognize what true knowing and numinous knowing truly are. If one recognizes them truly, one is a seasoned master of the Dao, and there is none who does not attain the Way. Alas! In the Way of the golden elixir, a deviation of a hair’s breadth leads to a mistake of a thousand miles. How many are those who truly recognize it?

[Li’s Explanation]
"Excellent" signifies beauty, the designation for the golden flower. Alchemists call true lead the "golden flower." As the *Cantong Qi* states: "The lead’s body is black without, yet harbors a golden flower within." From this black lead, one extracts white gold and pairs it with cinnabar mercury, thereby producing the primordial qi. This is precisely the "golden flower." Returning it to oneself yields the reverted elixir, yet the reverted elixir must first be preceded by refining the self. When the self is purely refined, the reverted elixir comes easily.

One who "forgets emotion in the face of scenery" has achieved mastery in refining the self. All beautiful scenes stir no emotion; one’s sole desire is to cherish this single point of qi—this true qi, called the moon’s radiance. Why is it also named the moon’s radiance? Because the moon’s fullness serves as a gauge for the qi’s condition. As the *Wuzhen Pian* says: "On the fifteenth of the eighth month, one delights in the toad’s glow—precisely when the golden essence waxes strong." This is identical in method to delighting in the moon’s radiance.

The moon begins to wax on the third day; Lu Yan likens this to tender qi. By the fifteenth, it is full; Lu Yan likens this to qi at its fullest. When qi is full, the golden essence waxes strong. The golden essence is the substance that appears within the moon’s radiance—same origin, different names. When it waxes, yellow sprouts fill the crucible, and white snow suffuses the sky. To the enlightened eye, it shines resplendent as a flower. The alchemist, wielding the sword that pierces heaven, gathers it, then applies fire at the proper time to refine the reverted elixir. This flower alone is the true prize.

One must never discard the true flower to pluck false gourds in the garden, lest one come to lament the error. Not only are gourds mistaken, but the five metals and eight stones are likewise false and not true. The myriad herbs and thousand formulas are all deviations, not the Way. What one seeks—neither false nor deviant—is this golden essence alone.

From whence does this golden essence arise? Observe the golden toad and the jade crow: these are its birthplaces. The toad, a yin creature of the water, is called "golden"—thus the true yang within Kan. The crow, a yang creature of the sky, is called "jade"—thus the true yin within Li. When true yin and true yang interact, they generate the qi of the two crescents. From the qi of the two crescents arises the true One qi. The moon’s radiance and the golden essence are both this same thing; one need only recognize it truly. If one recognizes it truly, one is a seasoned master, clear in fire times and discerning of lead.

[Liu’s Explanation]
Gathering the medicinal ingredients.

**[Li’s Words] Plucking the Yellow Flower.**
The rootless tree blooms with many flowers,
Scattered across the earth beyond the River of Love.
Hard to pluck—what can be done?
Step by step, walk into the Dragon-Tiger’s den.
Once the yellow flower is gathered and brought back to the cave,
Your name is inscribed in the Purple Palace, never to fade.
Laughing heartily, oh white clouds,
Prepare the celestial ladder to ascend to the Great Luo.

**[Liu’s Annotation]**
Throughout the cosmos, the qi of the Dao fills all;
wherever the light of true spirit shines, there the flowers bloom—
so many, scattered across the earth.
Yet though the flowers bloom everywhere,
people fail to recognize them before their eyes,
as if blocked by a river.
Though they wish to pluck them, it is most difficult,
and they can do nothing.
The difficulty lies in this:
the world’s people are all ensnared by fame and profit,
entangled by love and attachment,
abandoning the true to grasp the false,
mistaking suffering for joy.
Step by step, they walk into the perilous lair of Dragon and Tiger,
opposing the Way of life and destiny—
thus the flowers are hard to pluck.
But if a man of courage and resolve,
a man of decisive action,
casts off worldly ties,
seeks a teacher’s oral instructions,
and cultivates the true through the false,
then among the many flowers he may select and gather
the most central and correct yellow flower,
bring it back to the cave,
nurture it into the elixir,
and prolong life.
Then his name is inscribed in the Purple Palace,
never to fade.
The yellow flower is the flower of the central earth,
the yellow realm of Wu and Ji,
the most balanced and upright of flowers,
pure vital energy without impurity.
When this vital energy returns to the cave,
spring endures through all four seasons,
as if dwelling in a nest of white clouds,
carefree and at ease—
another realm beyond the human world.
How could one not laugh heartily,
knowing such joy?
At this stage, the returned elixir is attained.
Then, setting up the furnace anew,
reestablishing the cauldron,
one undertakes the work of ascent,
preparing the celestial ladder
to become a Great Luo Heavenly Immortal.

**[Li’s Explanation]**
The innate, original substance—
the worthy do not increase it,
the foolish do not diminish it.
Everyone possesses it,
everyone is born with it—
the flowers are many indeed.
Yet they are blocked by the River of Love,
causing the original to be buried.
Though the flowers bloom across the earth,
how can they be reached when the River of Love stands between?
The River of Love is the human heart of the posterior world of desire,
which obstructs the heart of the Dao of the prior heavens.
Once the heart of the Dao is blocked,
plucking the immortal flower becomes difficult.
What, then, can be done?
The immortal master tells the seeker:
There is no other way but to search step by step,
to inquire path by path,
crossing one mountain after another,
ford one river after another,
until entering the Dragon-Tiger’s den—
only then may one see the original truth.
This Dragon emerges from fire,
this Tiger is born from water.
From the posterior heavens, they exhale the qi of the prior heavens.
The Dragon hides in yin,
the Tiger hides in yang.
When yin and yang unite,
they give birth to Dragon and Tiger.
When Dragon and Tiger unite,
they give birth to the golden flower.
This golden flower lies in the southwest, the direction of Kun.
The earth of Kun is yellow,
so its flower is also the yellow flower.
If one can gather this yellow flower,
take it back to the cave,
and congeal it into the golden elixir,
then one’s name is inscribed in the Purple Palace, never to fade.
Laughing heartily—profound mastery is self-attained.
Oh white clouds—deep abiding in tranquility.
If one wishes to advance further,
to become a Heavenly Immortal,
one must set up the furnace and cauldron anew,
erect the celestial ladder,
to ascend as a Great Luo Heavenly Immortal.
Those who aspire to become Heavenly Immortals
may prepare the celestial ladder thus.

---

**Fourteen**
**[Liu’s Words] Yang Arises from Yin.**
**[Li’s Words] The Cauldron Produces the Medicine.**

The rootless tree blooms with fragrant flowers,
The lead cauldron glows warmly with treasure-light.
On the golden bridge, gazing toward the winding river,
In the moon, the sun is clearly seen.
Swallow the raven’s liver and the hare’s marrow,
Replace all the dust and old intestines.
In the realm of fame and profit,
In the land of love and attachment,
Never turn back—vain is all your toil.

**[Liu’s Annotation]**
The true spirit of the prior heavens,
where all virtues gather and all goodness converges,
emits the most fragrant qi.
When its fragrance is at its peak,
it is the moment when the lead cauldron glows warmly with treasure-light.
The lead cauldron is true knowing.
With true knowing,
one can cast off the old and embrace the new,
cultivate immortality and attain the true—
hence it is called the lead cauldron.
The treasure is the treasure of true spirit;
without true knowing, true spirit does not appear.
True knowing holds the heart of the Dao,
and within the heart of the Dao lies the true One qi of the prior heavens—
this is called true spirit.
When the lead cauldron glows warmly,
it is the balance of firmness and softness,
neither biased nor partial,
and the cauldron stands firm.
When the cauldron stands firm, the heart of the Dao manifests;
when the heart of the Dao manifests, the light of true spirit gradually arises—
this is called the appearance of treasure-light.
The golden bridge is metal;
the winding river is water.
Standing on the golden bridge and gazing toward the winding river,
one sees the image of metal within water.
Metal born from water—
yang arises from yin—
this is seeing the sun within the moon,
which is also the lead cauldron glowing warmly with treasure-light.
When the cauldron’s light appears,
yin and yang unite in virtue,
spirit and qi ride the moment in harmony.
Thus one enters the womb of creation,
holding it in place and not letting it depart—
this is swallowing the raven’s liver and the hare’s marrow.
The raven’s liver is green, the essence of the sun,
symbolizing the luminous nature of spirit-knowing.
The hare’s marrow is white, the radiance of the moon,
symbolizing the true emotion of true knowing.
Swallowing the raven’s liver and the hare’s marrow,
nature does not leave emotion,
emotion does not leave nature—
true and utterly luminous,
luminous and utterly true.
Nature and emotion become one,
true spirit never obscured,
round and complete,
radiant and bright,
pure and bare,
unadorned and free.
All posterior accumulations are purged,
the heart of the Dao abides,
the human heart is forever extinguished—
all the dust and old intestines are replaced.
Once the intestines are renewed,
all things become empty.
Fame, profit, love, and attachment—
what is there to cling to?

[Li’s Explanation]
This fragrance is neither perceptible nor foul—an utterly pure and pristine fragrance, the fragrance of primordial arising, unstained by the postnatal realm.

The lead crucible is the external crucible. The method for refining lead requires establishing an external crucible in the southwest, called the "Village of Kun" or "Mother Kun." The mother’s body is inherently empty and must rely on the father Qian’s solar essence to produce lead. This solar essence is the dragon’s mercury. The dragon, as the eldest son, takes the father’s place and enters the mother’s womb, where qi and essence intermingle, and the crucible of primordial true lead is thus established. Ancestor Zhong said: *"The great yang shifts into the moon’s brightness"*—this is the method of establishing the crucible. The following line, *"Within the moon, the sun is clearly seen,"* refers to this state of gentle warmth. When the lead crucible is gently warm, the treasure-light appears. This treasure-light is the light of the life-treasure; when it emerges, it is the primordial qi, a white image reflected above the brows and eyes. Ancestor Lü said: *"The lead crucible gently warm, light pierces the curtain,"* and again: *"Examine the space between the brows—there lies the sign."* This describes the same vision.

The golden bridge is the magpie bridge below, located on the path to the southwest, where the golden qi shines. The winding river is where qi encircles the magpie bridge, its light imprinting the southwest. Some of old interpreted Ancestor Lü’s line *"On the winding river, the moon’s radiance gleams pure"* as referring to the twelve curves of the small intestine—this is a descent into demonic delusion. Others have taken it to mean the space between the mouth and nose, an even graver fall into delusion. Only Master Chen Niewan said: *"On the southwest path, the moon’s radiance shines bright; the great medicine is born from this place. I recall an ancient verse: ‘Above the winding river, the magpie bridge spans.’"* This truly grasps the essence.

Why is this so? The southwest corresponds to *kun*, and *kun* governs the abdomen. Where the precious light appears, the moon’s radiance shines bright; where the moon’s radiance shines bright, the golden *qi* emerges. Thus, upon the golden bridge, one gazes upon the winding river, where the moon above the river shines directly upon the golden bridge.

The moon’s radiance gleams resplendent, and within yin, yang is born—hence the saying: *"Within the moon, the sun is clearly seen."* The sun is *taiyang*. The three-legged crow within the sun is the essence of the sun. To swallow the crow’s liver is to ingest the solar essence of the eastern direction; to consume the hare’s marrow is to partake of the moon’s radiance from the western direction. When essence and radiance are combined in ingestion, the great medicine is born. When sun and moon are both swallowed, the golden elixir takes form—thus the line: *"Swallow the crow’s liver and hare’s marrow, and the dust-laden old intestines are wholly transformed."*

What further attachment to love, fame, or profit could disturb this pure heart? Why turn back in thought, only to waste the day in vain? On the fifteenth, [Liu Yan] tends the furnace and applies the work.

[Li Yan] speaks of the work of *wenyang*—nurturing and refining.

The rootless tree bears flowers most fresh,
As talismanic fire sears mercury and lead.
At the furnace’s edge, visions arise—
Gathering all depends on the Dharma-boat.
The master’s hand, firm at the helm,
Lets the great waves churn the sea’s depths.

Cross the Three Passes, pierce the Mud Pill.
Early on, the nine apertures of the body are all opened.

[Liu’s Commentary]
The treasure of true love, once worldly dust is shed,
Becomes utterly pure and clear—how could its flowers not bloom fresh?
Yet their freshness depends entirely on the work of talismanic fire searing lead and mercury.
True numinosity is the essence of true knowing and numinous knowing;
True knowing and numinous knowing are the functions of true numinosity.
True numinosity divides into true knowing and numinous knowing;
True knowing and numinous knowing unite to form true numinosity.
To refine the lead of true knowing and the mercury of numinous knowing
Is to refine true numinosity itself.
Refining means using true knowing to govern numinous knowing,
And numinous knowing to align with true knowing.
When true knowing and numinous knowing congeal,
They restore the treasure of true numinosity—
The freshness of its flowers defies description.

Yet while true numinosity is easily formed, the firing times are most difficult.
As Master Ziyang said:
*“Though you recognize cinnabar and black lead,
Without knowing the firing times, it is all in vain.
The work depends entirely on the power of cultivation—
A hair’s breadth off, and the elixir will not form.”*

The Dao of the golden elixir requires gathering the medicine at the proper time
And refining it with the proper method.
Without knowing the time or the method,
Even if the great medicine is in sight, it will not be yours.
Thus, at the moment of tending the furnace,
Amidst the indistinct, forms appear;
Within the profound darkness, essence arises.
A single spark of true numinosity’s light
Emerges from the formless—
Seeming to exist, yet not existing;
Neither form nor emptiness.
Visions manifest—this is the moment the great medicine is born.

At this time, the Three Corpses, Six Thieves,
The Five Aggregates, and the Seven Emotions—
All manner of illusory visions—
May also appear before you.
You must steady the Dharma-boat,
Firmly grasp the helm,
Forget the visions, and remain unmoved,
Letting the waves churn the sea’s depths without wavering.
Through such effort, gradually gathering and refining,
Nurturing yang and restraining yin,
The longer you persist, the stronger the work becomes.
When the work is complete,
Essence transforms into qi,
Qi transforms into spirit,
Spirit transforms into emptiness.
Crossing these Three Passes,
The wind stirs in the Mud Pill,
The Dharma-body manifests—
And the yin qi of the body’s nine apertures is all transmuted.

The Three Passes are not the lower, middle, and upper *dantian* of the alchemical tradition,
But the three passes of refining essence, qi, and spirit:
Refining essence into qi is the first pass,
Refining qi into spirit is the middle pass,
Refining spirit into emptiness is the upper pass.
Crossing these Three Passes, spirit merges with the Great Void,
Moving freely without obstruction—
This is called piercing the Mud Pill,
For the Mud Pill Palace is where spirit is stored.
The nine apertures belong to the illusory body,
But once the Three Passes are crossed and the Mud Pill is pierced,
The Dharma-body is perfected.
The yin qi of the illusory body’s hundred channels and nine apertures
Is transformed into yang qi,
And every aperture shines with light—
Even the million and four thousand hairs
Become guardian spirits.
Students must not let words obscure the meaning.

[Li’s Explanation]
This chapter speaks of *wenyang*—nurturing and refining.
Wu Yuan’s interpretation—that crossing the Three Passes, piercing the Mud Pill, and opening the nine apertures refers not to the lower, middle, and upper *dantian* but to the three refinements after which spirit merges with the Void, moving freely, and the illusory body’s nine apertures all shine with light—is correct.
However, the preceding lines must be understood in the context of *wenyang*.
Otherwise, the stages of entering the chamber to return the elixir,
Nurturing the embryo, and shedding the husk
Would all be jumbled together,
Which does not align with the immortal masters’ intent of explaining each stage in turn.
Thus, this passage refers solely to *wenyang*.

“Fresh” means radiant—
The sign of deep *wenyang* work,
Renewing day by day, flourishing month by month.
“Talismanic fire” refers to the cyclical firing times:
At dawn, advancing the yang fire;
At dusk, retreating the yin talisman.
The *zi* hour is when yang is born, and fire should be advanced at *zi*,
But by dawn, it is the *yin* hour—
Why advance fire at *yin* instead of *zi*?
Because fire is born in *yin*, where yang qi flourishes,
So fire is advanced at this time.
The *wu* hour is when yin is born, and the talisman should be retreated at *wu*,
But by dusk, it is the *xu* hour—
Why retreat the talisman at *xu* instead of *wu*?
Because fire is stored in *xu*, where yin qi is concealed,
So the talisman is retreated at this time.
Retreating the talisman replenishes mercury;
Advancing fire draws out lead.
Lead governs mercury,
Mercury embraces lead—
Lead diminishes day by day, while mercury increases,
Hence the line: *“Talismanic fire sears mercury and lead.”*

“Tending the furnace” refers to the external furnace,
Not the furnace used when entering the chamber.
When entering the chamber to refine lead, a crucible is necessary,
But in *wenyang*, only the furnace is used, not the crucible.
Yet the furnace may be external or internal.
As Ziyang said:
*“Within, there is the natural true fire,
In the furnace, ever blazing bright red.”*
This is the internal furnace.
He also said:
*“For the external furnace, diligence in increasing and decreasing is key—
Nothing surpasses the true seed.”*
This is the external furnace.

At the furnace’s edge, wondrous visions appear—
Not the radiance of the treasure,
Nor illusory visions,
But the civil fire within and the martial fire without.
Civil and martial fires refine,
Gradually gathering, gradually adding.
The work of *wenyang* must not be interrupted.
It depends entirely on the Dharma-boat and the master’s hand,
Unshaken by wind or waves,
Undisturbed in its primal work.
Then the Dharma-boat sails boundlessly,
Coming and going without cease—
Like Bodhidharma carrying gold across the sea,
Directly reaching the other shore.
Hence the lines:
*“Gathering all depends on the Dharma-boat,
The master’s hand, firm at the helm,
Letting the great waves churn the sea’s depths.”*

The final three lines are already clarified in Liu’s commentary;
No further explanation is needed.

Sixteen
[Liu’s Note] Recognize true lead.
[Li’s Note] The singular true lead.

The rootless tree, its blossoms in full bloom—
Recognize true lead as the primal ancestor.
Essence, qi, spirit—one crucible refines,
Woman transforms to man, the old to youth.

To seize the White Tiger in the west,
First tame the Green Dragon in the east.
Like attracts like—strive well:
When the outer medicine flows, the inner medicine flows.

[Liu’s Annotation]
“In full bloom” speaks of luxuriance and abundance. Amidst the flourishing blossoms, good and bad, partial and true, mingle together. Only the true immortal blossom may be gathered and used. What is this true immortal blossom? It is true lead. This lead is the true emotion of true knowing, the manifestation of true numen. As true knowing is outwardly yin and inwardly yang—outwardly black, inwardly white—it is called true lead, or “gold within water,” or “lead of the watery realm,” or “flower within the moon.” Its names are manifold, yet all denote this single thing: true knowing. Only this true knowing contains the primordial true unity’s initial qi, the root of yin and yang, the source of the Five Phases, the seed of immortals and buddhas, the lineage of sages and worthies—the true primal ancestor of all who cultivate the Dao.

Once the ancestor is recognized and brought home, revered and upheld without a moment’s separation, essence, qi, and spirit naturally gather in the crucible, without need for force. For when the father returns, where would the child go? With the added work of talismanic fire and refinement, even a woman may transform into a man, even the old may become youthful. “Woman transforms to man” does not mean the body changes form; rather, a woman, being purely yin, through cultivation and refinement, transmutes yin into yang, becoming like a man. “The old become youthful” does not mean the face regains youth; rather, the old, their qi withered, through cultivation and refinement, return to the root and revert to the origin, becoming like a child.

Yet the way of woman transforming to man and the old becoming youthful, though it begins with recognizing true lead and true knowing, also requires first mastering the refinement of the self. If the refinement of the self is not thorough, true knowing will not come; even if it comes, it will not stay. Thus it is said: *“To lead the White Tiger from the western garden, first subdue the Green Dragon in the eastern home.”* The White Tiger belongs to the west and metal, symbolizing true emotion; the Green Dragon belongs to the east and wood, symbolizing true nature. True emotion and true nature are originally one family—why the need to lead or subdue? Because after their entanglement in the postnatal, the true is mixed with the false: true emotion becomes false emotion, kindness tinged with harm. Like a tiger leaving its den, it rushes west to wound others, no longer belonging to me but dwelling in another’s home.

Once true emotion becomes false, true nature is obscured and likewise turns false. The false takes charge, the true retreats, and nature and emotion fall out of harmony—like the dragon in the east and the tiger in the west, never meeting. To restore the true, one must first dispel the false; to lead emotion, one must first harmonize nature. Harmonizing nature is the work of refining the self. Refining the self means refining the nature of one’s temperament. When the nature of temperament is transformed, true nature naturally appears. With true nature manifest, unshaken and unmoved, true emotion also emerges. When true emotion emerges, false emotion does not arise, and the White Tiger may be led back to pair with the Green Dragon, emotion and nature entwined in love.

The White Tiger is the primal ancestor of true lead, differing only in name. Because true knowing is unyielding and strong, it is called the White Tiger; because true knowing is soft yet conceals strength within, it is called true lead. To lead the White Tiger is to gather true lead. “Leading” here is not by force but a leading without leading—when nature is settled, emotion naturally returns. This is simply the way of like attracting like, the resonance of yin and yang within and without. Nature presides within and belongs to yin—the inner medicine; emotion operates without and belongs to yang—the outer medicine. Yin and yang are originally one qi, nature and emotion share the same root. When the inner medicine flows, the outer medicine cannot but flow. Inner and outer in harmony, nature seeks emotion and emotion longs for nature. When nature and emotion unite, true numen congeals, and the symbol of the returned elixir appears.

The Pure Yang Elder said: *“When nature abides, qi naturally returns; when qi returns, the elixir naturally forms.”* The Purple Yang Elder said: *“To refine the ninefold transmutation, first refine the self and hold fast to the heart.”* Both speak of the necessity of refining the self before the elixir may return.

Alas! True lead is easy to gather, but refining the self is most difficult—the work of refining the self is truly great!

[Li’s Explanation]
“In full bloom” speaks of the intensity of emotion. Lead is the true lead within a person. When true lead manifests, its emotion is most intense. Simply recognize the true and gather it, and the golden elixir is immediately accomplished. For this true lead is the embodiment of the central yellow and upright position, the primal ancestor of the great elixir. Gather it to restrain mercury, and the three families meet to form the immortal infant. Extending this, thousands upon thousands, generations of descendants all trace their lineage to this true lead. Thus it is called the primal ancestor.

“Essence, qi, spirit—one crucible refines” describes the state after lead returns and mercury is subdued, the three families meeting. Yet to forge true lead, there is first the wondrous art of woman transforming to man and the old becoming youthful. The fire of the Li Palace is true essence; the water of the Kan Palace is true qi; between Kan and Li, there is the wondrous earth at work—true spirit, also called true intent. When qi and essence interact, with spirit presiding, gold is born in the water, mercury descends in the fire. With spirit maintaining balance, regulating excess and deficiency, through fierce refinement, the fire steams and the water boils, and gold rises with the water—this is the power of essence, qi, and spirit refined in one crucible.

When it enters the Li Palace, the fire of Li is extinguished by the water of Kan. It does not fly or flee. Qi is stabilized by spirit, essence is congealed by spirit. Lead and mercury both die, returning together to the fertile earth. The three families meet in the central palace, refined into a single purple golden elixir—this is the wondrous work of essence, qi, and spirit refined in one crucible.

When first the Eastern House’s son entrusted his form to the West, the Western Dui became the true Maiden, the Maiden acting in place of Mother Kun. Within the female crucible appeared the Thunder Male—thus the female transformed into male. This male is called the Third Lord of the Nine, young in years, truly the Dao Father of Wood Duke incarnate in the womb of the child. Hence Wood Duke is renamed the Duke’s Son, the old transformed into the youthful.

This Duke’s Son rides a white tiger, roaming the Western lands with fierce might. Once a Daoist saw and asked him, “You, the tiger-riding youth—are you the transformation of Wood Duke?” The youth, knowing the man’s heart held true awakening, dared not conceal the truth and answered, “Yes.” The Daoist then turned and laughed, saying, “The lead of the watery realm is but one flavor. Master Cui’s words are true indeed.”

Now, to summon back the Duke’s Son, one must first capture his white tiger, for the white tiger is the steed formed from the youth’s primordial qi. If you wish to journey west to seize the white tiger, you must first subdue the green dragon in the Eastern House. For the white tiger is the nature of metal; the green dragon is the nature of wood. When wood interacts with metal, fire arises within wood, and fire in turn compels metal to return. When metal merges with wood, water surges within metal, and water in turn extinguishes fire to stabilize it. These four, though distinct, are in truth the same—different in kind yet alike in essence.

Since they are of the same kind, employ your mysterious skill to bring them together. Thus, inner and outer unite, outer returns to inner submission, and when the outer medicine connects with the inner, the inner medicine likewise connects with the outer. This passage speaks only of true lead, not of true mercury, for where there is lead, there is mercury—though mercury is unspoken, it resides within. Hence it is said, “When the outer medicine flows, the inner medicine flows.”

Lead, qi, male, youth, tiger—all are outer medicine. Essence, female, elder, dragon—all are inner medicine. As for spirit, it abides between the inner and outer essence and qi.

Seventeen methods of gathering the firing timing.
Six gates of firing timing.

The rootless tree, its blossoms fair,
Heaven answers stars, earth answers tide.
The dragon-slaying sword, the tiger-binding cord,
Turning the Big Dipper’s handle, the Northern Asterism’s pivot.
Forging a crucible of true sun and moon,
Sweeping away three thousand six hundred paths.
Ascending cloud-laden skies, roaming free at will,
Sin, filth, and mundane dust—all erased with one stroke.

[Liu’s Annotation] The true spirit lies concealed within the postnatal, obscured by accumulated habits and guest qi. Its blossom is most difficult to unfold. Occasionally, when it does emerge, a single gleam of radiance pierces through the void—like a pearl, like dew—tender, delicate, and exquisitely fair. Its appearance is most fragile, as if opening yet not fully open. The primal qi, undifferentiated and whole, in heaven responds to the stars’ brightness (though not yet full), and on earth to the soil’s moisture (though not yet damp). The brightness of stars and the dampness of earth are both signs of yang qi’s initial stirring.

When yang qi first stirs, it is the tender moment of the true spirit’s blossom. At this very instant of fragility, the conscious mind may seize upon the spirit’s light to spawn delusion, scattering nature and shifting emotion. One must swiftly apply fierce firing and rapid refinement, nip deviations in the bud, and guard against subtle errors—nurturing yang while suppressing yin—to protect the treasure of life.

The dragon-slaying sword serves to curb the temper of qi; the tiger-binding cord serves to restrain delusive emotions. When the temper of qi does not flare, the true spirit manifests; when delusive emotions do not arise, true feeling is born. With true nature revealed and true feeling born, one revolves the Northern Asterism’s pivot and turns the Big Dipper’s handle, transforming killing into life and converting punishment into virtue. Thus can one forge and refine a crucible of true sun and moon.

The sun is the image of yang containing yin, an analogy for the numinous awareness inherent in true nature. This awareness is the female within the male, true yin. The moon is the image of yin containing yang, an analogy for the true knowing inherent in true feeling. This knowing is the white within the black, true yang. Forging and refining true yin and true yang—these two great medicines—returns them to a single qi, which congeals into the elixir. Swallowed and ingested, it extends life and reverses destiny.

This is the most sublime and wondrous Dao, not one of the three thousand six hundred heterodox paths that cling to emptiness or fixate on forms. For when the great Dao is accomplished, one ascends cloud-laden skies and roams freely at will, and all sins, filth, and mundane dust are erased with a single stroke. Those three thousand six hundred heterodox paths, however, merely tinker with the stinking skin-bag, only inviting more sins, filth, and mundane dust—how could they ever erase them?

[Li’s Exegesis] “Fair” describes the tender delicacy of the moment when the first yang sprouts. Heaven corresponds to the upper, earth to the lower. At the time of yang’s birth, a flicker of starlight appears above the brows (the ancients called this “heaven responding to the stars”), and a vast tidal qi surges within the abdomen (the ancients called this “earth responding to the tide”). Such are the signs of the medicine’s arising—this is no falsehood.

Master Wuyuan likened the stars’ brilliance in heaven and the dampness of earth to the initial stirring of yang qi, neither full nor moist, which is also a valid interpretation. Others cite *The Mirror of Entering the Medicine*, where “heaven responding to the stars” refers to the upper magpie bridge, and “earth responding to the tide” to the lower magpie bridge—both hold profound principles. Yet I have privately heard that “responding to stars” and “responding to the tide” pertain to aligning with the moon and the hour: the stars awaken one to the moon, the tide to the time. This is precisely the crucial firing timing of the great returning elixir.

I excerpt a few lines from the *Cantong Qi* as corroboration:
*“The metal reckoning is fifteen,
The water number is the same.”*

Before the furnace, fix the weight in two *zhu*,
Five parts water remain in excess.
When these two are taken as true,
The gold’s weight returns to its origin.
If the third enters, it will not do—
Two parts fire must accompany it.”

This is the true meaning of “responding to stars” and “responding to the tide.” The gold must weigh fifteen *liang* precisely because it aligns with the moon’s number, signifying the full vigor of metal’s essence. Over 5,048 days, the celestial *qi* first reaches completion, and fifteen *liang* of gold can generate fifteen parts of water—this corresponds to the first fifteen days of the lunar month. The water’s number matches the gold’s number, just as the tide’s number aligns with the stars’. If gold and water are insufficient, true water will not arise; this is what is meant by “heaven not responding to stars, earth not responding to the tide.” How then can one fix the weights?

To truly respond to stars and tide, take the first fifteen days of the lunar month as the standard. From new moon to full, count one and a half days as one part. Two such periods—three days—usher in *geng*. Only then does two parts of true water emerge: heaven responds to stars, earth to the tide. By the fifth day, it becomes three parts—three parts are unusable. By the eighth day, it reaches five parts—five parts are excessive. Neither aligns with the stars or tide.

Only when two parts of water are paired with two parts of fire does true alignment occur—this is the authentic response to stars and tide, the true sign of *kan* water. When gold first generates water, at precisely two parts, the source is utterly pure, possessing *qi* but no form: this is the *White Tiger’s* first channel. As the tiger exhales its breath, the dragon meets it with two parts of true fire, refining it into the elixir’s foundation.

As for the gold that generates two parts of water, it must wait until the fifteenth day, when the metal’s essence peaks and the water’s tide arises. This is the “two sevens’ period,” when true lead first descends—this is responding to stars and tide.

Some may ask: *Why must the fire be precisely two parts?*
Answer: In one hour’s work, divided into three *fu* and six *hou*, only one *fu* and two *hou* of fire are used. Thus, dragon and tiger remain balanced, devouring and being devoured in turn. At the critical moment, one must wield the sword to subdue the dragon and grasp the cord to tame the tiger. Circulating the *gang* and turning the Dipper, returning to the central palace, the sun and moon conjoin their essences. Refining and tempering them, the true Way is attained.

My teacher from Wuyi Mountain offers an even more precise and illuminating explanation, which I now detail here.

*Qian* heaven is yang; stars are heaven’s fire essence, yang within yin. *Kun* earth is yin; tides are earth’s water *qi*, yin within yang. Essence is the father of fire, *qi* the mother of water. When *Qian*-father and *Kun*-mother unite, *li* fire and *kan* water are born. Thus it is said: “Heaven responds to stars, earth responds to the tide.” “Responding” denotes the mutual resonance between them.

The *Cantong Qi* states:
*“Without stars and moon,
How could water be gathered?”*
From this, we know that when heaven’s light illumines earth, it responds with stars; when earth’s *qi* bears heaven, it responds with tides.

The immortals liken heaven’s stars to the fire within the human heart—fire is one’s nature, and nature belongs to the dragon. If it does not descend, the stars scatter and fire disperses. Thus, one must wield the dragon-slaying sword to subdue it; the sword represents great wisdom. They liken earth’s tides to the water within the human body—water is one’s emotions, and emotions belong to the tiger. If it is not tamed, the tide overflows and water flows unchecked. Thus, one must grasp the tiger-binding cord to subdue it; the cord represents great insight.

Great skill appears clumsy; great wisdom seems foolish. When insight and wisdom merge into darkness, the wondrous mind arises. To turn the *gang* and wield the Dipper’s handle requires the wondrous mind’s power.

The *gang* is the Northern Dipper. The Dipper governs life, residing in its handle. Wherever the handle points, life-giving *qi* arises. The human body’s wondrous mind, by moving the Dipper’s handle, can transform killing into life. As the Dipper’s handle revolves, the golden elixir enters within. When the golden elixir enters, the wondrous mind returns to me.

The wondrous mind is the true body, neither born nor destroyed, its virtue merging with heaven and earth, its brightness uniting with sun and moon—it is the true sun and moon within the human body. To seek the wondrous mind, one must return from the postnatal to the prenatal. First, cause the external sun and moon to exchange their light externally, mastering the firing times and understanding the *fu* and *ke*. Only then can it be attained. Upon its return, the internal sun and moon must exchange their light internally, shining ceaselessly day and night. By harmonizing and nurturing them, one forges a furnace of true sun and moon.

This is the wondrous secret of the golden elixir’s great Way, the profound mystery of the seven returns and nine refinements. It sweeps away the 3,600 side paths, allowing one to ascend the clouds and roam freely, erasing all karmic dust and worldly filth in a single stroke. Without understanding this great Way, there will never be a day of liberation. Karmic dust and worldly filth will only accumulate—how can one fail to awaken?

**[Liu’s Note]** Reverse the mechanism of *qi*.
**[Li’s Note]** Skillfully employ the art of theft.

The rootless tree’s flowers bloom high,
Ocean waves surge as the moon plays with the tide.
The Silver River’s path pierces the nine skies,
The raft’s shadow spans the void, striking the Dipper’s tip.
Touching the Weaving Maid’s loom stone,
Treading the Cowherd’s magpie bridge,
Entering the immortal court with bold courage,
Stealing the Queen Mother’s peaches from Jasper Pool.

**[Liu’s Commentary]**
The primordial great Way encompasses heaven and earth, governs the movement of sun and moon, and transcends all existence. Its flowers bloom so high they resemble the moon in the sky, its light reaching the ocean’s depths. Though ocean waves surge to the heavens, water cannot drown the moon’s light—instead, the moon plays with the tide. This is like a person in the sea of suffering: circumstances cannot harm their true nature but instead refine it through adversity.

Again, the Silver River’s path is distant, piercing the nine skies, yet humans cannot easily cross it. However, with a celestial raft spanning the void and turning the Dipper’s handle, one can traverse it. In ancient times, Zhang Qian rode such a raft across the Silver River and witnessed the Cowherd and Weaving Maid stars meeting—this serves as proof.

In terms of principle, the world also possesses its celestial raft, capable of crossing the Silver River. What, then, is this worldly celestial raft? It is none other than the Great Dao of the Golden Elixir. The Great Dao of the Golden Elixir operates within the void, capable of revolving heaven and earth, reversing yin and yang, seizing the workings of creation, and transcending the mundane to enter sagehood—this is the celestial raft. Yet the marvel of the celestial raft lies in the manipulation of the Dipper’s handle. The Dipper’s handle is the seventh star of the Northern Dipper, Yaoguang, also called the Celestial Stem. Where the Celestial Stem points is auspicious, where it rests is inauspicious, for where it points, the qi of life resides. In the instant the Dipper’s handle is turned back, yin and yang unite, and the sprouts of life emerge effortlessly—hence the saying: *“Grasp the Weaving Maid’s shuttle stone, tread the Cowherd’s magpie bridge.”* The Weaving Maid belongs to yin, the Cowherd to yang; the magpie bridge is where the Cowherd and Weaving Maid meet. By grasping the shuttle stone and treading the magpie bridge, yin summons yang, and yang comes to meet yin—when yin and yang unite, the Golden Elixir takes form. This principle is enacted within the waves, its workings performed in the void, enabling one to enter the ranks of immortals, with boldness of spirit, and steal the Queen Mother of the Jasper Pool’s peaches. The Jasper Pool lies in the west, and the Queen Mother is the ancient yin, the Mother of Earth. The peach is the Elixir, the single yang of the *Zhen* trigram. The Queen Mother’s peach is the image of *Kun* nurturing *Zhen* within; the Elixir resides in the west, but when stolen and returned to the east, it becomes one’s own, and the Elixir is restored. Yet the marvel of this restored Elixir lies in the union of yin and yang, and the marvel of their union lies in reversing the qi mechanism amidst the waves of the great sea, unmoving and unshaken. To remain unmoving and unshaken amidst the waves of the great sea is the mark of a man of bold spirit—what heaven among the nine skies cannot be ascended? What Silver River cannot be crossed? What Queen Mother’s peaches cannot be stolen? Those who cultivate stillness and forget form, acting only within quiescence, how could they know of this?

---

*[Li’s Explanation]*
"High" refers to the void. The surging waves of the sea are what Master Ziyang called the time when "the winds and waves are fierce, and the Mysterious Pearl is born." As the wind rises and waves surge, their sound shakes the void—hence "surging to the heavens." Yet the Mysterious Pearl, like a round autumn moon, appears upon the sea—thus "the moon plays with the tide." To reverse the flow of the Silver River and pierce the nine skies is like Zhang Qian riding the raft, its shadow spanning the void, the qi mechanism reaching its apex. Yet for the river raft to advance, there must first be guidance, lest the waters overflow their course and stray from the river’s path—this is why the Dipper’s handle serves as the mooring. The word "moor" is most apt: for mortals, mooring a boat means resting for the night, but for the immortal’s river raft, the Dipper’s handle is the anchor. To proceed straight and true, one cannot moor—yet to speak of "mooring the Dipper’s handle" is precisely to moor where one cannot, where one must not, mooring upon the Dipper’s handle. Following the Dipper’s revolution, movement contains stillness, death gives way to life—just as heroes and bold men act with unbridled resolve, their sails catching the wind without mooring, for this is the moment of grand resolution and great opportunity. Not mooring surpasses mooring, and mooring is as good as not mooring—such is the meaning of "mooring the Dipper’s handle."

The Weaving Maid and the Cowherd are the celestial yin and yang stars, meeting once a year on the seventh night of the seventh month. The Weaving Maid belongs to yin, the shuttle stone likened to mercury; the Cowherd belongs to yang, the magpie bridge the place where the Cowherd and Weaving Maid meet, the direction where gold and mercury unite. Above, the Dipper’s handle is mentioned; here, the Cowherd and Weaving Maid—thus the Dipper serves as their matchmaker. Without the Dipper, the Cowherd cannot meet the Weaving Maid; when the Dipper turns, the Cowherd crosses the river, and gold unites with mercury. As Ancestor Lü said: *“The work of advancing fire lies in the peril of the Cowherd and Dipper,”* and Niwan said: *“The marvel lies in the tail, the winnowing basket, the Dipper, the Weaving Maid, and the Cowherd,”*—both express this same idea. To grasp the shuttle stone is to have mercury receive lead; to tread the magpie bridge is to have lead and mercury travel the same path. From this, one’s heavenly fate is secured, and one’s aspirations can be fulfilled—one may encounter the immortal ranks and become bold of spirit. Why is this? Because one has stolen the Queen Mother of the Jasper Pool’s peaches. Wuyuan’s explanation—that the Jasper Pool lies in the west, the Queen Mother is the Mother of Earth, the peach is the image of *Kun* nurturing *Zhen* within, and the Elixir in the west is stolen and returned to the east to form the restored Elixir—is clear, yet the word "steal" is not as vivid as "thieve." To thieve the peach from the east is one matter; the *Kan* trigram as thief is another. To thieve the peach from the east is to go to the west to obtain gold; the *Kan* trigram as thief is to seek lead from the depths of water. How marvelous is the meaning of "thieve"!

---

*[Liu’s Words]*
Yin and yang wrestle and congeal.

*[Li’s Words]*
Giving birth to the Mysterious Pearl.

The Rootless Tree,
its flowers in full bloom,
Dragon and Tiger mount the altar for battle.
Lead enters mercury,
yin and yang unite,
the image of the Mysterious Pearl is priceless.
This is the true seed of one’s homeland,
restoring youth and prolonging life.
Ascend to heaven,
to the Land of Ultimate Bliss,
and escape the wheel of rebirth to meet King Yama.

*[Liu’s Annotation]*
The Golden Elixir is the image formed by the clash of yin and yang—thus the flowers must be in pairs to be of use. Yin and yang are the Dragon and the Tiger, lead and mercury. The Dragon is true nature, mercury is numinous awareness, also called the primordial spirit, both belonging to yin; the Tiger is true emotion, lead is true knowledge, also called the primordial essence, both belonging to yang. The Dragon and Tiger battling is the gathering of nature and emotion. Lead entering mercury is the congealing of spirit and essence. When nature and emotion gather, spirit and essence congeal, yin and yang unite, and the single qi blends—true numinosity becomes perfectly luminous, the Dharma-body takes form, round and resplendent, like a single Mysterious Pearl, a priceless treasure.

This treasure is no external object—it is the true seed of one’s own homeland, originally inherent, yet lost without trace after mingling with the postnatal. Now, with yin and yang harmonized, what was nonexistent is restored, what had departed returns. Planted in the homeland, with the root established the Way arises, generating endlessly, reversing aging to regain youth, extending life without limit, ascending to the heavenly realm of ultimate bliss, and escaping the suffering of rebirth.

[Li’s Exegesis]
The "pair" refers to the qi of the two crescents. When the qi of the two crescents unite, Dragon and Tiger mount the altar, mutually devouring and reflecting. "Battle" signifies this devouring. After a great struggle, Dragon and Tiger reach equilibrium: when the Tiger battles the Dragon, lead is cast into mercury; when the Dragon battles the Tiger, yin is matched with yang. When yang-lead and yin-mercury merge, this priceless treasure is born. As the *Awakening to Reality* states:
*"Tiger leaps, Dragon soars—waves surge rough,
At the central true position, the Mysterious Pearl is born."*
The Mysterious Pearl is the primordial singular qi, the original source of immortals and buddhas, the true seed of one’s own homeland, not an external thing. Veiled by the postnatal, it long ceased to manifest. Now, within the Dragon-Tiger altar, yin-mercury and yang-lead unite as true husband and wife, returning from within postnatal Kan and Li to the prenatal. Thus it is said: *"The Dharma-image of the Mysterious Pearl is beyond price."* From this true seed of the homeland, those who obtain it reverse aging to regain youth, prolong life, ascend to heaven, attain ultimate bliss, and escape the wheel of rebirth to avoid facing King Yama.

This speaks of the method of Dragon and Tiger, yin and yang, battling and uniting—one must seek its firing times in the annotation to the chapter *"When the Flower Is Most Radiant."*

[Liu’s Note]
The Elixir of Return is achieved in a single moment.

[Li’s Note]
The Returned Elixir’s nurturing and refinement.

The rootless tree—its blossoms most wondrous,
Cultivated in moonlight for but a fleeting moment.
With hands that seize the clouds, one ascends the cloud-ladder,
Plucking the first branch of the prenatal.

Drinking wine and wearing flowers, the spirit soars bright,
Laughing at the immortal elders sunk in drunken mud.
Entrusting the knowing heart, guarding with care,
Ever fearful the furnace’s firing time may flee.

[Liu’s Annotation]
The prenatal true numen, though nonbeing, gives rise to being;
though incomplete, it achieves wholeness—its blossoms most wondrous.
Yet what makes it wondrous is this: the prenatal, veiled by the postnatal,
vanishes without trace. Should one wish to cultivate it,
in but a fleeting moment it revives spring.
The marvel of this revival lies in plucking the first branch’s blossom.
The first branch is the ancestral qi of all life,
the numinous root that gives birth to heaven, earth, and humankind.
It does not fall into form, nor into emptiness;
concealed, it is true emptiness; manifest, it is wondrous being.
Utterly centered, utterly upright, utterly refined, utterly pure,
it flickers in the indistinct and obscure, like dew, like lightning.
It cannot be sought with intent, nor held with non-intent.
Sought with intent, one clings to appearances;
held with non-intent, one clings to emptiness.
It lies in settling the nature and forgetting the passions,
turning the light inward in reflection,
emptying to the utmost, stilling to the profound.
Not plucking, yet plucking; not taking, yet taking—
naturally, the true unity of the prenatal qi
arises from the formless,
congealing into a pearl like a grain of millet.
Within and without, radiant with light,
as if wearing immortal blossoms,
the spirit soars unimpeded, as if drinking immortal wine.
