Wearing blossoms, drinking wine—joy abounds therein,
unaware, unknowing, following the decree of the Lord.
One enters the realm of intoxication.

At this moment, the Returned Elixir has formed,
and the face of one’s birth-mother is seen anew.
No need for external furnace adjustments—
hasten to the inner furnace’s nurturing and refinement.
The numinous works in silence,
guarding with vigilance, the intent undivided,
ever watchful lest the firing time err.
The "knowing heart" is not an external knower,
but the heart that knows itself within.
The firing time’s swiftness or slowness, the heart knows of itself.
Knowing yet not deluded, the firing time does not err,
and the Golden Elixir ripens.

[Li’s Exegesis]
"Wondrous" means beyond human fathoming.
Not only humans cannot fathom it—
even yin and yang cannot fathom it.

If one could fathom it, then yin and yang would fail, intermingling in boundless obscurity—how then could one cultivate the primordial? That which is cultivated in the moon’s embrace: on the third day, when *geng* emerges, the medicinal substance is fresh and tender. Within this *geng* phase of the moon, one cultivates the golden flower, blending two parts fire with two parts water, stewing in primordial chaos for a moment—only then does the first primordial sprout emerge within the crucible. This is the work of a fleeting instant.

In that instant, when the first primordial sprout truly appears, the wondrous heart takes charge, immediately reversing the celestial pivot, soaring back across the Milky Way—this is the hand that grasps the clouds, the ladder that ascends them, the gathering of the first primordial sprout. The drinker of wine drinks this first immortal brew, and the primordial transforms into white nectar. The wearer of flowers dons this first immortal blossom, and the primordial returns with vernal yang. Flower is wine, wine is flower; to drink it and wear it is to have wine as one’s good companion and flower as one’s dear friend. The spirit and qi surge in harmony, utterly intoxicated—hence it is said, *"Drink wine, wear flowers, the spirit soars bright; the immortal elder laughs, drunk as mud."*

The "knowing heart" is the heart in accord, the wondrous heart within oneself. Vigilant guarding means observing the firing time with this wondrous heart. Yet guarding entails several aspects, and the furnace fire has two phases: if the firing time is insufficient, one withdraws and supplements with *zhun* and *meng* to protect it, requiring external furnace adjustments; if the firing time is complete, one guards it day and night with contained radiance, needing no external furnace adjustments. When the ten-month count is full and nine years have passed, the true person emerges from the crown of the head.

Otherwise, if the external furnace is removed prematurely when it should not be, the firing time will be insufficient and the elixir will not mature; if the external furnace is not removed when it should be, the firing time will be excessive and the elixir will surely be harmed. If the inner furnace is removed prematurely when it should not be, the firing time will not be refined and the elixir will lack potency; if the inner furnace is not removed when it should be, the firing time will stagnate in dullness and the elixir will not emerge. All these are errors in the furnace’s firing time. It is thus hoped that the knowing heart, through meticulous vigilance, will avoid such errors.

"Flying" signifies deviation—this should be read in light of the earlier chapter *"When the Flowers Truly Fly."*

[Liu’s Exegesis]
Harmonizing yin and yang.

[Li’s Exegesis]
Obtaining the medicine and returning the elixir.
The rootless tree, its flowers in true yellow,
is born in the central land of wu and ji.
The eastern household’s maiden, the western house’s youth—
as husband and wife, they enter the bridal chamber.
The Yellow Matron urges them to drink the ghee-wine,
each day growing drunk in a haze of intoxication.
This immortal formula, the soul-returning nectar,
raises the dead and revives the living—it is the King of Medicines.

[Liu’s Annotation]
Yellow is the true color of the central wu and ji. Wu, as yang earth, governs movement; ji, as yin earth, governs stillness. When wu and ji unite at the center, they form the true trust, also called the true intent. When the flower’s hue is true yellow, the true numen has entered the central, correct position. Yet for the true numen to be centered and upright, one’s nature and emotions must be as one. The eastern household’s maiden is the nature of wood; the western house’s youth is the emotion of metal. One nature, one emotion—paired as husband and wife, they enter the secluded bridal chamber. With the Yellow Matron urging them to drink the ghee-wine and harmonizing the firing times, what was not in harmony must harmonize, and once harmonized, it remains so. The ghee-wine is not the dregs of the mundane world, nor is it the tangible substances of essence, fluids, or blood within the body. It is the qi of intermingled yin and yang in harmonious union, coalescing into the true unity of essence, flowing as the true unity of water—fragrant and sweet in flavor. The ancients called it "jade liquid," "nectar," "sweet dew," or "ghee," all terms that describe this single point of harmonious qi. To "urge drinking" means to regulate what is not harmonious until it reaches perfect harmony. In the practice of the Dao, when yin and yang attain perfect harmony, one remains constantly responsive yet still. From afar, one observes phenomena, yet phenomena are no longer phenomena; up close, one observes the body, yet the body is no longer the body; inwardly, one observes the heart, yet the heart is no longer the heart. Unknowing and unperceiving, one follows the decree of the Emperor. Daily, one drinks the ghee-wine and enters the realm of intoxication. This intoxicated delight is the immortal’s formula, the soul-returning nectar—able to raise the dead, able to revive the living. It is the great King of Medicines. "Central," "wu and ji," and "Yellow Matron" are all alternate names for the true trust. In terms of yin-yang harmony, it is called "central"; in terms of yin-yang movement, it is called "wu and ji"; in terms of yin-yang harmonization, it is called "Yellow Matron"; in terms of activity, it is called "true trust"; in terms of stillness and stability, it is called "true intent." Thus, one thing has many names, but in sum, it is merely the one true trust. Recognizing this trust, one must apply solid effort upon it. First, seek emotion through nature; then, return emotion to nature; then, harmonize nature and emotion; then, merge nature and emotion into oneness, forming a single true numinous treasure. From beginning to end, nothing succeeds without this one trust—how great is the function of trust! When reduced to its essence, the centered and upright true numen is the union of nature and emotion. When nature and emotion unite, the true trust resides within. When the true trust manifests, nature and emotion naturally do not separate, and the true numen is naturally centered and upright. These three depend on and yet give rise to one another.

[Li’s Explanation]
Yellow is the true color, the correct awakening of the Buddhist school, the correct qi of the Confucian and Daoist traditions. In the Buddhist canon, it is called "yellow flowers"; in the immortal classics, it is called "yellow sprouts." Yet there are two kinds of yellow sprouts: one is the new medicine of the third day, the other is the great medicine of the fifteenth day. As *Awakening to Reality* states: "Where yellow sprouts arise, kan and li conjoin"—this refers to the new medicine of the third day. Where yellow sprouts arise is where kan and li should unite to plant the second yellow sprout. *Awakening to Reality* says: "Plant the yellow sprout, and it gradually grows"—this is the second yellow sprout, the great medicine of the fifteenth day. The growth of the yellow sprout truly arises from the union of kan and li. This union of kan and li occurs in the central land of wu and ji. The center is where essence and qi coalesce; the land of wu and ji is where movement and stillness harmonize. Once harmonized and coalesced, in an instant, the yellow sprout is born from within—hence it is said, "born in the central land of wu and ji." This yellow sprout has many names; in this chapter, it is the western house’s youth. The western house’s youth is the qi of metal; the eastern household’s maiden is the essence of mercury. Gathering the qi of metal to subdue the essence of mercury—this is the Dao of returning metal and mercury, the pairing of husband and wife entering the bridal chamber. Once in the bridal chamber, the Yellow Matron must guard them. The Yellow Matron is the "knowing heart" mentioned in the previous chapter. If the couple fears discord, their spirit, intent, and qi will struggle to enter the realm of harmony, and the elixir will not form. Thus, the Yellow Matron must attend to them, urging them to drink the ghee. The ghee is the essence of external nurturing warmth, the qi of internal harmonious union. The Yellow Matron is the intimate confidant; the firing times in the furnace will naturally not err. Between dawn and dusk, she urges them to drink frequently, each day growing drunk in a haze—truly a joyous affair. This wine is not mundane wine but the wine brewed by the immortal’s formula, called the soul-returning nectar. It can raise the dead and revive the living; neither minor nor external medicines can compare. It is the King of Medicines. This chapter describes the work of the fourth firing time after seeking lead in the second firing time. Seeking lead is an external affair: on the third day, when the moon emerges in geng, one applies effort. This is called "pairing water with fire," "the dragon approaching the tiger," "yin meeting yang," "li uniting with kan," "nature harmonizing with emotion," "mercury investing lead," "the maiden marrying the man"—all methods of using the postnatal to generate the prenatal. In sum, it is the union of essence and qi, an external medicine. Its work lies externally, requiring only one talisman and two firing times to establish the foundation of the elixir.

The Reverted Elixir.

This is an internal affair. One applies effort at the time of the full moon on the fifteenth day, calling it "using water to extinguish fire." This water is the water of celestial menses. It is also called "the tiger marrying the dragon," where the tiger is the tiger of the western direction; "yang subduing yin," where yang is the yang containing the true; "kan filling li," where kan is the prenatal kan; "emotion returning to nature," where emotion is the emotion of metal; "lead restraining mercury," where lead is the lead of True Unity; "the man pairing with the woman," where the man is the pure qian; "using the prenatal to restrain the postnatal." In sum, it is the union of true qi with true essence—an internal medicine. Its work lies internally, requiring two talismans and four firing times to congeal the Golden Elixir.

All this has been left undifferentiated by the ancients; here I expound it in detail, that when reading elixir scriptures, one may clearly distinguish between the two medicines.

Twenty-two
[Liu’s words] Congealing the Sacred Embryo.
[Li’s words] Capturing and subduing the Fiery Medicine.

The rootless tree, its blossoms now bright,
The moon’s yin essence presses close to the sun’s yang spirit.
Golden Crow’s marrow, Jade Rabbit’s essence—
These two things captured and simmered in one place.
Yang fire and yin talismans divide at midnight and noon,
Bathing rites added at the gates of mao and you.
Guard the Yellow Court, nurture the Valley Spirit,
A man conceiving an embryo—how laughable it seems!

[Liu’s commentary]
The prenatal true numen, its original luminous body,
Pierces heaven and earth, illuminating all—this is the blossoms’ brightness.
What makes it bright is the harmony of yin and yang qi.
A person’s singular self is purely yin, like the moon’s darkness without light.
Only by borrowing another’s deathless method does yang arise,
As the moon borrows sunlight to become bright.
The moon’s yin essence pressing close to the sun’s yang spirit—
Yin and yang in union—can, at the heart of heaven, shine brilliantly.
This is the merging of true knowing and numinous knowing,
The image of the true numen unobscured.

The Golden Crow’s marrow is the sun’s yang spirit,
In humans, the feminine within the masculine—
The true yin of numinous knowing.
The Jade Rabbit’s essence is the moon’s yin essence,
In humans, the white within the black—
The true yang of true knowing.
Earlier, it spoke of crow’s liver and rabbit’s marrow;
Here, it speaks of crow’s marrow and rabbit’s essence—
There is a great distinction; they must not be viewed as the same.
For crow’s liver and rabbit’s marrow are the medicinal substances of the Reverted Elixir,
The true knowing and numinous knowing of yin and yang yet to unite but on the verge of union—
Thus, the liver of the crow, the marrow of the rabbit.
Crow’s marrow and rabbit’s essence are the medicinal substances of the Great Elixir,
The true knowing that can be numinous, the numinous knowing that can be true—
Yin and yang already united and in harmony—
Thus, the marrow of the crow, the essence of the rabbit.
Yet to unite but on the verge of union is forced effort,
The false returning to the true.
Already united and in harmony is natural function,
The true becoming even truer.

Gather these two true medicinal substances and knead them into one,
Refine forth the yang within yang,
Then apply the fire-tending of zi, wu, mao, and you—
Thus is the Golden Liquor Great Elixir perfected.

Yet what is called zi, wu, mao, and you
Is not the zi, wu, mao, and you at the edge of the sky,
But rather the zi, wu, mao, and you within the body.
When true knowing appears, it is zi;
The method is to use firm advancing fire to stir the true knowing forth from the mysterious.
When numinous knowing arrives, it is wu;
The method is to use gentle retreating tally to draw the numinous knowing into the feminine.
When true knowing advances to the central equilibrium, it is mao;
The method is to ice-bathe this central equilibrium so it does not advance excessively.
When numinous knowing retreats to the central equilibrium, it is you;
The method is to ice-bathe this central equilibrium so it does not retreat excessively.
This is the Dao of tally-fire and ice-bathing,
An unchanging method for ten thousand ages.
If one applies effort according to the zi, wu, mao, and you at the edge of the sky,
One strays far indeed.

When tally and fire are not in error,
When bathing aligns with the proper time,
Yin and yang respond to each other,
Neither leaning nor tilting—
The Mysterious Feminine is established,
And the Valley Spirit arises within it.

The Yellow Court is the central and correct position,
The single aperture amid the union of yin and yang,
Also called the Gate of the Mysterious Feminine.
When primal yang and feminine yin unite, yin and yang merge,
This aperture exists;
When yin and yang are askew,
This aperture does not exist.
Where this aperture exists, there is the Valley;
Where there is the Valley, there is the Spirit.
Where this aperture does not exist, there is no Valley;
Where there is no Valley, there is no Spirit.
The Valley is the Yellow Court.
Yellow is the color of the center;
Court means emptiness.
Because it is empty within, it is named the Yellow Court.
Empty, it is numinous;
Numinous, it is Spirit—
This is called the Valley Spirit.

Observe the mountains:
Two cliffs stand facing each other,
Between them a valley.
When one calls out, the valley echoes—
This echoing sound is the Valley Spirit,
Commonly called the "cliff baby."
When human yin and yang unite,
A Spirit dwells within—
It is just like this.
Yet if one has not reached the state where yin and yang unite,
There is no center,
No Valley—
How can a Spirit reside there?
Only when yin and yang truly unite
Does a center appear,
Does a Valley form,
And the Spirit arise of itself.
This is what is meant by "the primal qi comes from the midst of emptiness and nothingness,"
By "true emptiness yet containing wondrous existence,"
By "to keep the Valley Spirit from ever dying, one must rely on the Mysterious Feminine to establish the root."

When yin and yang merge into one qi,
The Valley Spirit abides steadfast in the Yellow Court—
This is called "a man conceiving an embryo."
To "guard the Yellow Court" is to guard the center.
To "nurture the Valley Spirit" is to embrace the One.
Guarding the center and embracing the One,
After ten months the work is complete,
A body exists beyond the body,
And one endures as long as heaven and earth.

These are true and real dharmic signs,
Works accomplished within emptiness,
Not wrought from form and appearance.
Those who fiddle with circulation techniques on the stinking skin-bag,
Falsely hoping to form the sacred embryo—
How could they know what makes the Valley Spirit the Valley Spirit?

[Li’s Explanation]
Brightness is the arising of the Great Medicine,
The empty chamber giving birth to white,
Radiating great luminosity—
The time of great awakening, great enlightenment.
This Great Medicine is the yang within lead,
The gold within cinnabar,
The primal within the primal—
Like the moon’s dark essence at the heart of heaven,
Pressing close to the sun’s yang soul,
Forming a radiant orb of light,
Not like the sliver of the third day,
Far at the sky’s edge,
Near as the crescent brow.

The word "pressing" is crucial—
It means intimate closeness,
The two refining each other in one place.
Sun and moon unite as jade discs,
The sun’s yang soul pours entirely into the moon’s dark essence,
A thousand miles of brightness,
The heart of heaven gleaming like snow.
Seize the two and refine them together—
Not seizing the Golden Crow and then the Jade Hare,
But seizing the Golden Crow to grasp the Jade Hare,
Seizing one thing to thereby seize both.
At the moment of seizing,
There are the four phases of zi, wu, mao, and you, the fire at the gates.
Thus the Golden Crow flies into the Palace of Broad Cold,
And with the marrow of the Golden Crow,
The essence of the Jade Hare is harmonized.
Then the essence of the Jade Hare
Is entirely transformed into the marrow of the Golden Crow—
Only then is the moon’s dark essence pressing the sun’s yang soul,
Skillfully refined in one place.

At this time,
The yang soul is full,
The yin essence formless—
Two things become one,
One thing contains two.
Yin is exhausted, yang is complete,
Great luminosity radiates—
Thus it is called the yang within lead,
The gold within cinnabar,
The primal within the primal.
At this stage,
It is the Great Medicine of Golden Liquor,
And one applies the work of ingesting it according to the four phases of zi, wu, mao, and you—
Only then is it the Great Return Elixir of Nine Revolutions.

What time is zi?
When yang arises, it is zi—
Thus one advances the yang fire.
Where is wu?
When yin descends, it is wu—
Thus one retreats the yin tally.
Ice-bathing means natural adjustment,
Neither hurried nor slow.
This work should be applied
When the yang fire approaches mao,
When the yin tally approaches you—
Thus yang does not exceed firmness,
Yin does not exceed softness,
Firmness and softness attain the mean,
Entry and exit are in proper measure.

Formerly, Master Tao Cuncun elucidated the secret of fire-tending in the *Triple Concordance*,
And recorded his teacher’s *Fire-Tending Song* in his commentary.
I deeply admire it,
And now append it here as corroboration.

The song says:
"I recall my immortal elder’s Daoist methods,
All were those moves of our own house.
Originally there was no adding or withdrawing at zi and wu,
How could there be rabbit and chicken, punishment and virtue?
Ask: When is my zi?
Answer: At the time the medicine arises.
Ask: When is my wu?
Answer: When the medicine faces the Golden Gate.
Ask: When is my mao?
Answer: When the Red Child stands in the Cave of Fire Clouds.
Without the Guanyin Who Saves from Suffering,
The Great Medicine would surely burst.
This is the time for bathing—
Beyond this, the boat and oars of the Yellow River.
Again ask: What is the you gate?
Answer: When the Conception and Governor Vessels unite."

At this moment, if there is no Yellow Skirt,
How can the medicine attain primal auspiciousness?
Beyond this lies the *xu* treasury—
Pray inquire into the treasury’s secrets.
This is the mind-to-mind transmission of the One Thread,
The Supreme Dao requires no other seeking.”

When the medicine arrives at the *mao* gate,
One must employ the stillness of Guanyin.
Guanyin’s stillness governs with strict restraint,
Preventing the Red Child from seizing power—
Then sweet dew arises.
As for the *you* gate,
It is wrapped in the Yellow Skirt,
Preventing the primal pearl from spilling—
Then the white fluid congeals.
Such is the wondrous use of ice-bathing.

The Yellow Court is the center.
The Valley Spirit is emptiness and numinosity.
Abiding in the center to nurture emptiness and numinosity,
The Dharma-body manifests its image—
A man resembling a woman with child,
Laughable yet endearing indeed.

**Twenty-Three**
*[Liu’s words:]*
True emptiness, Dharma-form.
*[Li’s words:]*
Perfect penetration, self-so freedom.

The rootless tree,
Its blossoms now crimson—
Pluck all the red blossoms, and the whole tree is empty.
Emptiness is form, form is emptiness;
Discern true emptiness within form.
When true emptiness is fully realized, form vanishes,
Yet the Dharma-form endures, never falling into emptiness.
Named Perfect Penetration, called the Great Hero,
Nine generations ascend beyond the nine heavens.

*[Liu’s commentary:]*
The Great Dao of the Golden Elixir takes as its destination
The transcendence of all phenomena in soundlessness and scentlessness—
How could blossoms possess crimson hue?
If even the slightest trace of color remains,
The postcelestial qi and temperament are not yet fully transformed,
And the Great Dao remains unaccomplished.
The ancient immortals said:
“Not a shred of yin qi may remain if one is to become immortal.”
For if a shred of yin qi remains,
A shred of yang qi is incomplete,
And the true spirit may still suffer damage—
This cannot be called the Great Elixir of the sevenfold return and ninefold restoration.
The cultivator must pluck all the red blossoms,
Eradicating the adventitious dust-roots accumulated since beginningless kalpas,
Returning to the state where all things are empty,
Restoring the soundless, scentless visage prior to parents’ birth.
Yet this “emptiness” does not mean the lifeless stillness of wood or stone.
There is a Dao of borrowing the provisional to perfect the real,
And using the real to transform the provisional—
Hence: “Emptiness is form, form is emptiness;
Discern true emptiness within form.”
To be wholly without mind is to cling to emptiness;
To harbor even the slightest mind is to cling to form.
“Emptiness is form” means it is not empty;
“Form is emptiness” means it is not form.
Neither empty nor formed, yet both empty and formed—
This is true emptiness abiding within form.
“When true emptiness is fully realized, form vanishes,
Yet the Dharma-form endures, never falling into emptiness”:
True emptiness, once realized, settles all matters.
Originally without form,
Yet since form vanishes, the Dharma-form remains;
And since the Dharma-form remains, it cannot fall into emptiness.
Because it is true emptiness, the Dharma-form exists;
Because the Dharma-form exists, there is no form—
No form, yet Dharma-form abiding:
Thus emptiness is true, and truth is emptiness.
When cultivation reaches the point where true emptiness bears the Dharma-form,
And the Dharma-form preserves true emptiness,
The wondrous existence of the One Spirit,
Perfectly penetrating the Dharma-realm,
Becomes an indestructible vajra-body—
Water and fire cannot assail it,
Blades and weapons cannot harm it,
Tigers and rhinoceroses cannot wound it—
And it is called the Great Hero.
Not only does one ascend to the ranks of immortals,
But even nine generations of ancestors rise to the heavens,
Becoming deities together.
In former times, when Śākyamuni Buddha cultivated the sixteen-foot golden body,
And his Dharma-form dwelled in the Hall of the Great Hero,
It was this very Dao.

*[Li’s explanation:]*
Red is the symbolic form of the Great Medicine.
The immortal master’s *Daoist Sentiments Song* and *The Rootless Tree*
Are both essential works—
From them, this may be understood.
The *Daoist Sentiments Song* says:
“Of all phenomena, none are of the same kind;
A single red radiance is the utmost truth.”
When red radiance appears,
Its blossoms are crimson;
When the red blossoms are in hand, the true medicine is obtained.
Apart from these red blossoms, no medicine can be gathered.
Once the work of gentle nurturing is complete,
Furnace and crucible are entirely set aside—
All those blossoming trees are no longer discussed.
Thus: “Pluck all the red blossoms, and the whole tree is empty.”
Once the blossoms are empty, my Dao is attained;
Once my Dao is attained, emptiness is no longer empty.
Since emptiness is no longer empty, emptiness is form;
Form is not substantial form—it is the form of the Dharma.
Discern that true emptiness is not empty,
And true emptiness abides within form.
This “form” is not the form of form,
But the form of the Dharma.
When true emptiness is fully realized, form vanishes entirely;
When form vanishes entirely, the Dharma-form endures forever.
The enduring Dharma-form is true emptiness not empty.
“Perfect penetration” means merit and practice are complete,
All dharmas are penetrated,
And the substance and function of true emptiness are perfected.
Once called Perfect Penetration, one must be called the Great Hero;
Once called the Great Hero, one must become the patriarch of immortals—
How could nine generations of ancestors not ascend,
Rising together beyond the nine heavens?

**Twenty-Four**
*[Liu’s words:]*
Return to the formless.
*[Li’s words:]*
Attain the rank of the Three Purities.

The rootless tree,
Its blossoms now formless—
Without appearance or shape, hard to depict.
Nameless, yet responsive to call,
Seized and placed within the alchemical furnace.
Ignite the Samādhi fire of the microcosmic orbit,
Temper true emptiness to return to the Great Void.
Visit the immortal capital,
Receive the celestial tally—
Only then is one a true man, a great hero.

*[Liu’s commentary:]*
The treasure of the primordial true spirit
Is fundamentally empty,
A single qi harmoniously blended—
How could there be blossoms?
Without blossoms, without form or image,
It cannot be depicted or drawn.
If it cannot be depicted or drawn,
How could it have name or surname?
Yet though nameless and surnameless,
It is utterly empty and utterly numinous—
Still and unmoving,
Yet responsive when stimulated,
Like an echo answering a call:
Within true emptiness, the wondrous exists.
With this marvel of responsiveness,
One seizes the moment of resonance to act,
Placing it within the alchemical furnace of the Three Fields,
Using the true fire of Samādhi to temper and refine it to perfection.
From true emptiness, one may return to the Great Void.

The Dao returns to the Great Void, where emptiness itself is empty—nothing remains but the One True. There is no other thing.

The Three Fields are not the common alchemical terms for *qi*-sea, Crimson Palace, or Muddy Pellet; rather, they are the Elixir Fields where the Three Treasures—essence, *qi*, and spirit—converge. This is called the Gate of Primordial Transformation, also known as the Primordial Pass, the Central Yellow Court, the Alchemical Furnace, the Altar of the Great One, or the Gate of Wuji. In sum, it is the Cavern of Emptiness.

The treasure of the primordial true spirit governs the Three Substances—essence, *qi*, and spirit. When the true spirit is restored, the Three Substances are likewise restored. They transform of themselves, harmoniously blending in undifferentiated unity. First, from nonbeing they create being; then, from being they return to nonbeing. The refinement of true emptiness is precisely the marvel of transforming being into nonbeing. When being is thus transformed into nonbeing, both form and spirit attain perfection, merging with the Great Void in oneness. With merit and practice complete, one ascends to the Immortal Capital to receive the celestial mandate, becoming a Perfected One of the Ten Poles and the Great Primal Chaos—a true man whose great work is fulfilled.

*In Praise:*
Revealing the hidden depths of Laozi and Zhuangzi,
Continuing the heart-transmission of Zhong and Lü.
Unveiling the wondrous principle of the primordial,
Cleaving open the tangled paths of empty suspension.
The crucible’s right and wrong distinctly judged,
The medicine’s truth and falsehood plainly seen.
Emptiness and form blend into a single *qi*,
Hard and soft match as two strings in harmony.
Ah!
The alchemical method’s beginning and end fully disclosed,
The fire-tally’s advance and retreat wholly inscribed.
Twenty-four verses of the immortal’s formula—
Whoever grasps them becomes a deathless immortal.

*[Li’s Commentary:]*
The word "nonbeing" carries forward the meaning of "emptiness" from the previous chapter, deepening it to conclude the twenty-four verses. To refine the elixir to the point of emptiness is already perfect, yet if one clings to the notion of true emptiness, the notion of dharmic form remains. Emptiness still falls short of nonbeing. As Lord Lao said: *"Observe emptiness as empty; emptiness itself is empty. What is emptied is already nothing; even nothingness is nothing. Abiding in utter stillness."* Only this is the great liberation, the great awakening, the great purity, the great perfect enlightenment. Why? Because the wondrous being of utter stillness appears as emptiness, and emptiness as nonbeing—beyond all form, beyond depiction or illustration. Precisely because it is formless and imageless, it is difficult to depict or draw; it simply abides in utter stillness.

Before this, in gathering the primordial, there were those named after metals—gold for essence, yellow for the sprout, white for the primordial. But this utterly still true reality has no name or surname. Though nameless, it responds to every call, like an echo in an empty valley, answer following answer. Question it with words, and it receives the command as if facing you—this is the utmost subtlety in the world. Still and unmoving, yet responsive when stimulated—this is the utmost spirit in the world. Why? Because this utterly still true reality is hidden within nonbeing.

The principles of sages, worthies, immortals, and buddhas penetrate the workings of creation. Within nonbeing, being is concealed. At this stage, the uncanny and wondrous manifest—such as Leng Qijing, Zhang Jinghua, and Immortal Zhou Dian. Our Master Sanfeng, embodying the Dao, must seize nonbeing with nonbeing and enter the central realm of emptiness. Through great creation and transformation, within the furnace he circulates the true fire of Samādhi around the celestial sphere, refining and tempering until the dharmakāya of emptiness returns to the Great Nonbeing.

The Great Nonbeing is the realm of the sagely perfected—such as the Jade Purity’s Primal Chaos Great Heaven or the High Purity’s Crimson Primal Nonbeing Great Heaven. Those who refine the immortal Dao receive only the ranks of the Great Purity. But those who return to the Great Nonbeing first pay homage to the Dao and its Power, then to the Jade Emperor, and finally to the Primordial Beginning, attaining the fruit of the Three Purities.

The word "return" signifies that all foolish men and women are originally beings of the Three Purities. Yet due to karmic delusion, they descend age after age, remaining foolish men and women, unable to regain the realm of the sagely perfected. If they turn their hearts toward goodness, seek the Dao, and find a teacher—progressing from foundation-laying and self-cultivation through the seven reversals and nine returns, refining to emptiness and then to nonbeing, and from nonbeing returning to the Great Nonbeing—they once again become guests of the Three Purities.

Yet refining true emptiness requires the true fire of Samādhi around the celestial sphere. The celestial sphere does not refer to the river chariot but to movement within the heavens, the subtle workings in the void, the profound and mysterious transformations of the Dao’s natural law. Samādhi does not refer to yang fire but to the union of heaven-one and earth-two as three. Within heaven and earth, I establish the crucible and furnace. Spirit and *qi* merge in obscurity—this is the fire of immortal refinement, the celestial primordial elixir.

With merit complete and practice fulfilled, one ascends to the Three Heavens, visits the Immortal Capital, receives the celestial mandate, and may be enfeoffed as a Perfected Lord, an Imperial Lord, a Heavenly Venerable, or appointed as a master of the Five Peaks, the sacred mountains, the grotto-heavens, or the blessed lands to select immortals. Only then is one a true man, the greatest of men—divine to the utmost!

*In Praise:*
Scattering flower-rain across the sky,
Spreading golden earth below.
Hand clapping fish-drum and clappers,
Mouth singing the immortal hymns of the Upper Grotto.
Delivering the four continents,
Eternally embodying the Dao’s sentiment.
Ah!
Wherever one awakens to the true spirit,
First hold fast to our school’s essential intent.
The mountain man proclaims the true formula by the book,
Broadly opening the nondual gate to deliver the world.

*[Original Notes:]*
Wu Yuan said: "I do not know what tune this is."
Hanxu said: "Those who sing *Daoist sentiment* are called *pulling dark clouds*."
In the *Wuyuan* annotated edition, "subtle" is written as "precarious," which also conveys the sense of decline.
In the *Wuyuan* annotated edition, "green" is written as "pure," yet "green" signifies the freshness of new growth, akin to purity untouched by defilement.
"Wall-top" is written as "jade flower," and "jade flower" as "wall-top"—I have seen both versions.

This annotation interprets "wall-top" with depth, so I follow it.
⑸ *Fixed*: The *Kongqing Cave Heaven* edition of *Wu Gen Shu Er Zhu* writes it as "wisdom," which is correct.
⑹ *Original Note*: The *Wuyuan* annotated edition writes "又向" as "旋趁," differing in character but identical in meaning. However, "才经" is written as "残经," which some interpret as human desires—thus "gathering" is meant to repel the yin thief—yet this risks compounding error with error.
⑺ *Original Note*: The *Wuyuan* annotated edition writes "对景忘情" as "月月开时."
⑻ *Original Note*: The *Wuyuan* edition writes "爱" as "碍," which is inferior.
⑼ *Original Note*: Refers to the later phrase "raven’s liver."
⑽ *Original Note*: The *Wuyuan* annotated edition writes "浓" as "秾," "擒" as "牵," and "方" as "圆," though the meaning remains unchanged.
⑾ *Spirit*: Based on context, this likely should be "nature."
⑿ *Original Note*: The *Wuyuan* annotated edition writes "泊" as "斡" and "盗" as "窃."
⒀ *Original Note*: The *Wuyuan* annotated edition writes "产在" as "色正."
⒁ *Original Note*: The *Wuyuan* annotated edition writes "金花" as "红花," which is preferable, so I follow it. "灭" is mistakenly written as "法."
⒂ *Original Note*: The *Wuyuan* edition writes the two characters "中间" as "三田," though *Wuyuan* still interprets it as the wondrous aperture within.

*Sixth Scroll: Daoist Sentiment Poems, Lyrics, and Miscellaneous Writings*
By Changyi Mountain Man Li Hanxu
Collated by Chen Yingning of Wanjian

**Daoist Sentiment Poems (Twenty-Four)**

Men say it is good to be human,
I say being human is endless toil.
Even if wealth and rank mean nothing to me,
Must I still yearn day and night for the immortal isles?

As for me,
Hánxū is a Daoist.
Born into this world uncommon,
Yet my rebirth was amiss.
From childhood, I mumbled a few words,
And in adulthood, I was tangled in vines,
Dreaming of fame that would echo through ages,
Or of soaring as an immortal on earth—
All these fancies left me with nothing achieved.
Fortune’s five phases align,
And by grace, I still have a thatched hut,
Three fellow Daoists,
Roaming carefree, high above the mortal dust.
Laughing and smiling,
We linger among streams and stones.
Late autumn, early winter,
With no affairs in the mountains,
We brew a pot of chrysanthemum wine,
Admire the early plum blossoms,
And softly chant Daoist poems.

Alas, since descending into this world,
I recall my past life as a cold scholar,
Lightly drifting in a boat between Húnán and Húběi.
Why did I vow to seek the Western Paradise?
Wandering through clouds, waters, mist, and mountains.

And pity those born into this world,
Who enter the womb and lodge their souls,
Each layer of parents bestowing kindness.
Their faces resemble their fathers and mothers,
Nurtured with warmth and tender words.
Born as human—this is fortunate,
But one must know to cherish it.
After ten thousand kalpas and a thousand rebirths to gain a human form,
One must understand the causes sown in the great kalpa.

The Pure Yang Ancestor’s compassion is boundless,
Urging us to value this body before us.

Those who cultivate the Dao—
Not a speck of mundane thought may arise.
Hear my recitation:
Spring water is muddy when it leaves the mountain, clear within it;
I regret my past journey into distant lands.
Suddenly seeing so much splendor,
Only then do I realize how hard it is to remain unmoved by circumstances.

Those who cultivate the Dao—
Where does the Dao-heart arise?
The melody of wind and springs winds through ten thousand pines,
Yet it cannot compare to the ten-mile expanse of a tranquil lake.
The moon hangs at the heart of the sky, the cold rests in the water,
Suddenly cooling the mind’s earth.

Cultivators of the Dao—
The superior begin from nothing to create being.
My family’s elixir method comes from Yíngzhōu,
Starting with emptiness and nothingness.
Fear not the absence of signs,
For one must seek the root in nothingness.

First, refine essence into qi.
On the yīn qiāo vessel, qi drifts hazily,
So much true essence lies within.
Gather it into emptiness and refine it into qi—
A path opens to Pénglái’s distant shores.

Second, refine qi into spirit.
Spirit and qi merge into the boundless,
Suddenly hearing the true scripture chanted in the void.
The five directions, the five qi swirl around,
Announcing the birth of the spirit from the primordial azure.

Third, refine spirit to complete nature.
The immortal qi must be sought in stillness,
Few on the red-dust path understand.
Sitting in the central courtyard for three months of fragrance,
A golden sprout grows an inch deep.

Those who leave the household—
After refining essence to generate qi,
Some effects will appear.
Daily, guide the qi to the mud-pill palace,
Sweet nectar gradually fills the tip of the tongue.
Irrigating the three fields, nourishing the hundred vessels,
Naturally, essence grows and the valley spirit is at peace.

When sweet nectar fills the mouth each day,
The immortal heart arises.
On a jade isle, dwelling in seclusion,
The Pure Yang Ancestor sits high in a painted pavilion.
Sweeping the floor, burning incense—utterly idle,
Only the flower studio’s leisure remains.

With the immortal heart comes stillness of mind.
Deep in misty mountains, one lingers.
From this, literary thoughts turn to elixir refinement.
Sleeves rolled with white clouds, returning to the cave abode,
Head bowed, eyes closed, seated on the rush mat.

With stillness of mind comes the true heart.
All that is known and perceived is false;
Only the unknown and unperceived give birth to truth.
A single somersault shatters the primordial chaos,
And one sets out to become a Daoist in the Eastern Realm.

When the true heart appears, the true seed is ever-present.
Gold meets wood, mercury lingers,
The infant and the maiden meet—how joyous!
Last night, the Lady of the Cinnabar Terrace sent a sweet dream,
And a red pill was conceived.

Why is it called "from being to non-being"?
Congeal the jade liquid into elixir wealth,
Place it in the Kūn palace—truly still.
Suddenly, a single yang rises from the earth,
The elixir’s resources return to me without guesswork.

Why is it called "from non-being to being"?
True lead emerges from the great void,
Planted in the Lí palace, born in the Kǎn palace.
I see the golden sprout burst forth in luxuriance,
While others speak of white snow filling the emptiness.

Why is it called "joining for long life"?
Mercury’s nature is light and fond of flight,
Lead’s essence is heavy and never fails to consume.
In refining the elixir, if passion returns to nature,
One will surely ride a green phoenix into the Tàiwēi realm.

Why is it called "life within killing"?
Lead meets mercury in distress, yet bestows grace within harm,
Mercury, bound by lead, is reborn from death.
If the wondrous treasure lacks restraint,
The work of immortality will not be perfected.

How does one meet the Green Maiden and give birth to the sacred embryo?
The Green Maiden is young and adept at cultivation,
Not a solitary yīn—her body cannot generate life.
After meeting in the bridal chamber,
They share a bed for ten months to bear the embryo.

How does one transfer the cauldron and shift the embryo, so the child begets grandchildren?
The Great Dao ascends step by step,
Once the returned elixir is achieved, one meets the immortals.
Year by year, the fire’s timing adds to the household,
Gazing toward Pénglái, the spirit soars.

Hear the mountain man speak of the wondrous principles of nurturing life—
There is much joy in them.
I wonder, in ordinary times, which masters and immortals did you admire?
The Pure Yang Recluse, old Chén Tuán,
A carefree immortal of the Five Dynasties.
The joy of the clapper and fishing rod beyond the world,
Unmoved by chaos, naturally at peace.

And which immortal master did you follow?
The Great Yuan’s remnant elder, known as Sānfēng,
Who vanished at the end of the Yuán dynasty.
Only when the Chéngpíng era arrived did he reappear,
Delighting in drifting clouds and flowing waters among lofty pines.

As for me, the carefree Hánxū of the Daoist sentiment poems,
These twenty-four chapters express it all.
In Chángyǐ Mountain, there is nothing else—
A single fish-drum, a single lyric.
To restrain the heart is the method; Daoist sentiments dispel cares.

If you wish to ascend to the Great Luó Heaven,
You must refine your heart.

Abandon thoughts of fame and fortune, sever ties to profit and desire.
Even if gossamer threads of calculation arise, fierce fire burns them away to reveal the celestial nature.
One end rises, one end severs—
Only subtraction is seen, no addition.
Fear not the ten thousand restless "heart-monkeys," nor the thousand galloping "mind-horses."
Practice internal work, breathe into the dantian.
Guard the true breath, and purity comes naturally.
Plunge into profound darkness to draw forth auspicious mist.
It tingles my Crimson Palace, intoxicates my limbs with languid softness.
This is my true method for taming dragons, my technique for slaying serpents.
Passed down everywhere among mortals, the celestial mechanism is not sold for silver.
Wealthy disciples present gifts in homage; impoverished disciples follow fate as it comes.
They remain unfeigned, I remain incorrupt—
Now, after three years of digging the well, I seek to establish some karmic merit.
Who could know the perversity of destiny, the hardship of the times?
Family fortunes decline, heroic spirit wanes, and the elixir furnace is utterly neglected.
Yet should the winds of fortune shift one day, I’ll cast off all and roam carefree to the immortal isles.

**The Heart-Mind Chapter**
Its heart-mind luminous, its functions manifold.
Its spirit profound, its substance serene and steadfast (I act not, yet qi naturally coalesces).
Thus the ancients directly grasped the "non-spiritual spirit" as the true spirit.

**Cultivating the Heart-Mind**
Sweeping away resentment and desire is no hardship;
When the heart-mind is at peace, the body too is at peace.
The moon casts its clear light upon still waters,
The wind carries coolness around the winding balustrade.
Buddhist scriptures penetrated, vexations vanish;
Daoist teachings attained, a steadfast vision arises.
Ever restrain the heart-mind within the chamber of the chest,
Walking alone, sitting alone, pacing alone.

**Three Poems on Emptiness**
Practicing is easy, attaining is hard—
Apart from emptiness, no elixir is made.
If the world seeks a place to stabilize the tripod,
Within this realm, the expanse surpasses the heavens.

Loving is easy, delighting is hard—
Apart from emptiness, no elixir is made.
If the world seeks where the life-nourishing medicine grows,
Within the gourd, the immortals’ altar already stands.

Attaining is easy, preserving is hard—
Apart from emptiness, no elixir coalesces.
If the world seeks where to establish destiny,
From beginning to end, it is all one undivided whole.

**Cultivating the Elixir**
Massage and daoyin techniques,
Easy to encounter, hard to perfect.
The Great Dao of the Golden Elixir,
Hard to encounter, easy to practice.
Practicing is not without difficulty,
Yet it can be aligned with longevity.
Modeled on heaven and earth,
Tempered in nature and emotion.
Nature and emotion interact,
Echoing through the empty valley.
Manifestations transform and change,
The work lies in stillness and clarity.
Heart-mind clear, qi clear—
Beneath the earth, thunder rumbles.
Thunder shakes heaven and earth,
The two phases unite in true essence.
Dragon and tiger wage a great battle,
In the wild, supreme peace is established.
The three yang open the myriad apertures,
Gathering medicine into the central camp.
From this, for ten months,
The gentle fire nurtures the fetal immortal.
Splitting open the mud-pill peak,
Carefree, one ascends to the Jade Capital.

**Discoursing on the Art of Immortality**
Of old, there were gods who did not die,
But no bodies that did not die.
Those whose spirit attains non-death
Are precisely those who attain immortality.
When mortals die, their spirit perishes;
When immortals die, their spirit endures.
The gulf between endurance and perishing spans heaven and earth,
Immortals and mortals are not of the same rank.
In the world, centenarians
May endure many springs.
Yet as old age approaches,
Their true nature grows dim and lost.
Bewildered by avarice and desire,
Their will and vitality fade into stupor.
Before death, the body is already in chaos;
Before rebirth, past causes are obscured.
Not waiting for the next life,
They sink into ruin before their very eyes.
Who can embrace this wondrous art?
Dwelling in leisure, refining the primordial spirit.
Even if one cannot escape death,
The numinous nature alone transcends the dust,
Roaming carefree between heaven and earth,
Playing the flute in the wake of Lü Dongbin.

**Lamenting the Pass of Sensual Desire**
Through the ages, the greatest fools
Love beauty as they love flowers.
Through the ages, the most foolish
Are insatiable in their greed.
Indulgence in desire harms the essence,
Like a violent gale stripping the forest of its blossoms.
The *Guo Feng* warns against sensuality,
Yet still, there is a touch of elegance.
The dissolute revel in desire,
Their kind no better than swine.
Those who cultivate both sensuality and the Dao
Meet ruin and lamentable ends.
Better to take a fair maiden,
Sever desire, and refine cinnabar.
How wondrous was Zhang Guolao,
Who tended garden melons with his wife.
How illusory was Yi Yongchang,
Who sang of clouds and mist with his spouse.
Both sages were enamored of beauty,
Yet in the world beyond, their love was rare.
The perfected have no lustful thoughts,
The root of desire is severed, never to sprout again.
I admire the immortals of old,
Whose celestial consorts were their true partners.

**Those Who Cultivate the Dao Should Sever Desire**
The Great Elixir employs the furnace and cauldron,
Metaphors for refining and nurturing the medicine.
The vulgar, failing to understand, heap scorn and slander—
This is the fault of clinging to literal words.
In jest, I mimic their phrasing
To clarify the meaning for the rigidly conventional.

Fourteen ounces of refined gold
Can forge the immortal’s crucible.
Take the lead within *gui*,
To mend the losses within my body.
Crimson silk nurtures the true nature,
The alchemical chamber holds fine vessels.
Once the work is complete, all are discarded,
Selecting companions for shared cultivation.

There was a young man from the eastern household,
In the prime of his years, keen and perceptive.
Kan and Li inverted and overturned,
Nature and emotion mutually affirmed.
These are my numinous parents,
Together entering the grotto-heaven to seclude themselves.
When the Dao is perfected, a family of immortals,
The Great Luo will come to welcome them.

**Matching the Rhymes of Master Ma Bicheng’s "Declining Health in Prosperity"**
The year of the Boar ends, the Rat begins,
Winter’s start already reveals spring.
The first yang returns to its origin,
Myriad things gradually contain the new.
Snow-covered earth, rivers and mountains gleam,
Frost-laden sky, the atmosphere is true.
In the cold garden, fine fruits ripen,
Tangerine wine reveals the spirit’s fullness.

**Awakening at Dawn**
Ten thousand matters fail to go as wished,
Returning, I chant poetry again.
This body should be singularly good,
My Dao is not entirely mistaken.
Spring arrives swiftly, swallows come early,
The night is cold, the cock crows late.
The morning star is as large as a bowl,
Few know the celestial signs.

**After the Double Ninth, Inviting Disciples to Roam the Muyi Hermitage**
Emptiness congeals into emerald, following the azure vastness,
Clapping hands, singing as we ascend.
I wish all beings to ascend the realm of longevity,
Where the immortal spring is truly fragrant for the elderly.

**Double Ninth at the Yang Zheng Residence**
On the Double Ninth, the sky drizzles like silk,
In the Hall of Nurturing Integrity, the wine cup is raised.

**Jade Wine and Shared Resonance**
Jade wine intoxicates, yet one remains unaware,
Fine words await guests, few truly understand.
Only you and I share this tune in harmony,
Knees pressed close, hearts converse in wondrous speech.
When shall we ride twin white cranes together,
Beneath Green City Mountain to seek the magic lingzhi?

**To the Tune of "Man Jiang Hong" – First Variation**
Clapping hands, singing aloud,
I sigh—mortals flicker like candle flames,
Laughing at lives spent in vain, deaths in futility,
What resolution can there be?
The arena of fame and profit stretches wide, yet battles yield but emptiness,
The debts of poetry and books weigh heavy, faces seek elixir formulas.
When shall you roam the seas and skies, Master?
Permit me to speak.

Parents still live, yet home is hard to leave.
Debts of gratitude run deepest, ties are hardest to sever.
Loosen the reins of fame, return instead to the thatched hut.
Millet and beans bring joy as we till the verdant fields,
Mountain cups toast longevity with golden chrysanthemums.
Only when I’ve served the white-haired elders
Shall I make my final decision.

**To the Tune of "Man Jiang Hong" – Second Variation**
Pray tell, esteemed sirs,
What does it mean to cultivate immortality or Buddhahood?
First, one must thoroughly grasp the Confucian classics,
Then we may speak of this together.
Nurturing nature and preserving the heart embrace the wondrous Dao,
Cultivating the body and establishing destiny transmit the true formula.
Within vastness, the elixir is refined,
Riding the dragon forth.

When heaven’s fortune prospers, sages are nurtured.
When the lord’s Dao flourishes, talented ministers arise.
Laugh at our own carelessness and sloth—
Why offer uncut jade?
Who in this world has exhausted all worldly achievements?
The winds and waves of mortal life are boundlessly treacherous.
Better far to serve the mountains and forests,
And withdraw early.

**To the Tune of "Man Jiang Hong" – Third Variation**
The eight-legged essays and literary works
Are but dregs of the Six Classics.
Worse still, slick and glib tones are added—
Where is the truth in any of it?
The fawning postures of the times are truly laughable,
The rush for fame—why so frantic?
Relying on poetry and prose to become a high official,
To build a family legacy.

First, the learning is flawed,
Power once grasped, greed takes hold.
Weighing copper coins heavily,
While soldiers and common folk are cast aside.
If only there were a clear-sighted official who discerned right from profit,
Yet without silver to offer, even he becomes an enemy.
See how our kind, emerging from the mountains, must
Hastily retreat.

**Nine Characters of the Great River’s Western Lineage**
The Western Dao connects,
The Great River flows east,
The sea and sky stretch boundless.

**Inscription by Patriarch Lü**
The Great River’s first patriarch is Pure Yang,
After nine cycles, the elixir is perfected, the Dao’s qi flourishes.
Today, the transmission of the heart holds no other words—
May each of you steer the vessel of compassion.
